O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book, which is the last of the science of medicine, together with its fullness, and have made the end through its expositions and its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is very difficult in our region and is strange throughout, the science is lost and cut off, and nothing remains of the powerful ones except the small descriptions in the books of the ancients that hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and understanding is closed and the science is distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I want to give it life together with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of fire cautery irons, and other instruments of the work with the addition of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason of this, that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is distanced.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who undertakes this must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the arrangement of the limbs, and their forms and junctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles and their number, and the movement and the flowing and resting veins, and the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore Hippocrates said that knowledge without practice is much, and with practice is little; and especially in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things must be careful not to fall into error and kill people; thus, I have often seen many of those who meddle with this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and without experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who opened an abscess of scrofulous matter on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of the neck; therefore, so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another man who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; he also took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the sick man and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if it was cut, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another man who took on the case of a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and this man, full of ignorance, pressed the break onto the wound with tight bandages, and did not at all leave any slack in the wound, and left it like that for a while; and he told him not to loosen it at all; and it remained like that until the leg became completely swollen, and the foot, and it came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and untie the leg; and when I had untied it, it was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But nevertheless, the corruption had already been confirmed in the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another man who lanced an infected abscess, and then inflamed it further through the badness of his work.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is full of melancholic humor, it is not right to touch it with iron if it is not in such a place that one can entirely remove what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, good son, you must know that the work of the hands is divided into two divisions: namely, a work in which there is danger in several ways; and I will show you in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, you must guard yourself, so that foolish men cannot speak ill of you. Take up your weapons with caution, and undertake your sick people gently and firmly, and use the best way so that, through the grace of God, you may come to safety and be praised; and leave the frightening illnesses to the serious [doctors]. Remove your weapons from those who cause you fear and be strong in yourself so that you may go from this world to the other in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on a serious illness as a cure, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is on cauteries by fire and cauteries of acute medicine, and it is arranged from the head to the feet; and on the forms of instruments, and the tools of cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is on cutting and piercing, and on cupping and wounds, and on the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is arranged and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is on restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is arranged from the head to the feet, and on the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary for me to describe the quality of help and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest speech and subtle science and hidden secret; and many wise men spoke of this, and agreed on this; and their words are of little use to me, for I dread the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally to every complexion where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion with matter, some disagreed and said that cautery is a great help; and others said the opposite: that cautery is of no use for an illness coming from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat a hot illness by heat, nor by dryness; and whoever says the opposite says that cautery is a great help to a hot and dry illness that comes to the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it sometimes by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, let no one interfere except those who have tested it, and who know through long use the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the time period; for other complexions, we are not fearful, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians gathered together and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the part that is inflamed, and does not harm other members much.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines spread from one limb to another, and cause serious illnesses in the limb; and perhaps kill the patient.  Fire, because of its strength and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and the length of service and study I have put into the art, and it was based on the truth of things; and for this reason I apologize for the length of my speech, for I do not want to deprive you of the secret contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels illnesses from the body, just as the philosopher said in demonstrating it; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and chose springtime.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the ensuing harm is overcome with the help of cautery; and especially if the cauteries are for necessary pains, urgent and fast, than cannot wait for the time when greater harm might come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think about it, dear son, as fools do; for the illness cured by cautery has no return; and they say it thus; but it is not as they think, because cauteries are only medicines that change the complexion and dry up the humours that are the cause of pain, and are worth more than other medicines for the speed of its power and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And a powerful thing is that the illness sometimes comes according to the complexion of the sick person and the location of the illness and its strength; and superfluities are gathered in it through the consumption of food and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in a place where there is little superfluity and moisture, like cauteries on teeth for toothache and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worth anything after other medicine, but their intentions are wrong, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we have tried various cures for an illness, and they are of no value, then we apply cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and not according to the intention of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery is better than iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and the high nature of its substance; and they said that the cauterized area does not cause rot, but this is not true, for I have experienced it and found it to be true in some people; and gold cautery is better than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly; and if you heat it too much, it will damage the fire; and thus there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use iron cautery because we have found it more suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet, so that the way might be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two types, one used for a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and especially for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a resolving medicine, purifying the head for three or four nights, according to the strength and age and custom of the patient; and then cover the head of the sick person.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his thighs; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and let your middle fingers come to, then warm the cautery that is called "olivare," of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the location marked with ink, and move your hand slowly downwards and increasingly tight, rotating it; then lift your hand quickly and look at the area if you see the bone just a little; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that, take a pinch of salt, put it in water and soften cotton within, and place it on the area and leave it for three days; after that, put moist cotton in butter; and leave it until the burning is gone; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason, they aid it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should leave the cautery until part of the bone is burned, and then the burned part of the bone should be removed and treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one should leave the cautery on for a long time, and press so hard that one breaks off a piece of bone as large as a spindle that women use in their thread to allow the humors to come out; and the wound should be left open for a long time; then it should be treated and stitched.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem to me to be entirely good, except perhaps in some people where there is fear; and I seem to want to leave it; because the shoulder is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other limbs; and especially when the patient's shoulder is weak by nature, and the first semblance of cautery is safer and more gentle for me, and from this I use it in a manner that combines safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain affects the entire head and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie," and head cleansings, oils, and plasters; and if the cautery we have previously described is applied, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is strong and not too cold; then cauterize beneath that cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, apply cautery to each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and apply one cautery to the place called "vasselz"; and it is a place where leeches are applied; and ease your hand so you do not go down to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries on the horns should be more delicate than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in a part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head has been cleansed with purifying medicines, and the other treatments I mentioned in the division of illnesses have been performed, and none of this helps: then apply cauteries according to two methods, namely, with sharp medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries with sharp medicine are done thus: take a clove of garlic, peel it and slice it a little on both sides, and then pierce the temple where the pain is in such a manner that you can place the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it is placed, bind it and hold it tight, and leave it like this for twelve hours; and then untie it and remove the clove of garlic, and leave the wound thus for two or three days; then apply a cloth dipped in butter until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment treatment, until it is healed; and if you wish, do some of the burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery with iron is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "close" because the head is made in the shape of a closure, where there is a small curve, and a small appearance in the middle; and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and turn the iron slightly, until half of the thickness of the skin is burned; and remove your hand so that the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and a great deal of blood flows out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterwards, place cotton in vinegar water, and put it on the area for three days; then place cotton moistened with butter, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this headache with the cautery called "cultellare," use the whole point, and be careful not to cut the artery in this headache, which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a headache, as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not work, and you see that the previously mentioned cauteries of medicine and iron do not suffice, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and then cut a line of half a finger's length on the painful area, and remove your hand once, and be careful not to cut the artery and not to reach the bone; and watch out for the jawbone that moves when one chews, and the nerve does not move, and that spasms do not come to the patient, and watch out for the bleeding of the artery when it is cut, or the cut causes great fear, especially to those who do not know about it, and are not students and experienced; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it belongs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and one has tried soluble medicines and other treatments as we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not change, then heat this cautery, which is called "poins," of which this is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, prick all around the diseased ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place to prick; and there should be ten pricks around each ear; after that, treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that should be treated with cautery is only effective for those caused by phlegm, as we have stated in the divisions of diseases; and do not use cautery for those that arise from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When treating this type of torture caused by phlegm, and purges of the head and gargles, are ineffective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little outside the temple, and the third at the juncture of the two lips; and place the cautery on the apparently healthy part, and cauterize it on the head of the ear, a little below the horn of the head, and another on the temple, as long as a finger; and leave the cautery there until half of the skin is burnt; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the scalpel we have described before, but it is a little more subtle, and the knife should be slightly thicker; after that, treat the area as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When the apoplexy is longstanding and you treat it as we have described, and it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one where the place called "vessel" is, as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills that cleanse the brain; afterward, wash the patient's head thoroughly and apply a mustard plaster to the occiput, as described in the treatment of plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is thus healed, it is good; and if not, apply three cauteries from the middle of the head descending down to the neck, and let there be an inch between each cautery; and treat him as the others, and if you wish to add more, and the patient can endure it, apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and treat him until he is healed; and let the cauteries be called "olivare," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed with herbs and what we have previously said; afterward, wash the patient's head, then apply a cautery to the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is damp and the patient can endure it, and the illness is severe, apply four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave them until most of the skin is burned, and remove your hand; afterward, treat him until he is healed, and let the cauteries be called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of the epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not use cauteries except for those who are phlegmatic, and the brain must first be cleansed with herbs and other treatments that we have discussed in the section when the patient is severe and able to endure taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot endure it, give them gargles and chewing to cleanse the brain frequently with good foods; afterward, wash their head in the middle, and apply one cautery according to what we have said before, and one cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is severe and able to endure it, apply cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped, according to the manner I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply one subtle cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and the phlegm is thick, then cauterize with the types of cauteries as we have described for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities are declining into melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give them to drink things that cleanse the brain, according to what is stated previously in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, wash the patient's head; afterward, make a linen tourniquet, like a circle, and place it on the head; and the patient sits cross-legged, held securely from all sides; afterward, apply the liniment, and take melted bear's fat; and warm it gently by fire, so that the patient can endure it when placed on the head; afterwards, empty the circle within the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with other good treatments, until they are healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize it by making multiple punctures with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery softens the brain evenly; and then apply cotton soaked in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the water of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water comes first to the eyes by the signs I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something that purifies the head, and protect him from all moisture, and make him sweat in a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, command him to raise his head, and cauterize within the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of water is into both eyes together, or into one if the descent is into one; and cauterize across all the veins and arteries under the skull, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and watch out for any excess of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision the caution how you will stop it; and sometimes cauterization or incision is done under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are long-standing and habitual and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are on the outward appearance of the head's exterior; and one sees that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then make the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning of the water descending into the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or incisions under the two bones; and if more is needed, then wisely cauterize above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does no good, then give the patient three nights' worth of draughts; after that, rest the head, and make a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery; and make two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" above the two eyebrows, a little below the hair; and be careful not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the skin of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish, make two cauteries above the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not leave your hand there except until the third part of the skin is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are turned inward, and prick the eye, and cauteries are made according to two manners: that is to say, of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in a comfortable position; afterwards, draw a figure on the skin of the eyes that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put moistened cotton in egg white and a mixture of parsley on the eye, then heat the cautery of which this is the shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize over the figure you have drawn, little by little many times, until the heart is burned in that spot; and the sign of the healing of the work is that you see the skin retracted and the hairs raised at the puncture of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the burn is removed; then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs grow, and the skin is softened, then begin the cautery again on that same spot, as you did at first; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the skin is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medical cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make a shape of a myrtle leaf from parchment; then take French soap and hot water, of each one a certain amount, and grind them together well; and do it quickly, so that it does not cool, then spread it over the shape you have made, like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin of the eyes; and if the patient has only one eye affected, then one should work on one, and if on both, then in the same way; and place cotton moistened in egg white under the eye; and the patient's head should be in a comfortable position, and place your index finger on the medicine, and press it slightly and move it every time the patient feels the medicine biting, because it bites just like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the biting sensation has passed, remove the area of water, and examine to see if you see the skin raised as if it had been raised by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is like this, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then put more medicine on the area where the medicine hasn't worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are aligned; then apply moistened cotton in butter until the burned area is healed, then treat the area with ointments called "diafenis" and others until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary, be very careful in your work to prevent any medicine from getting into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the skin becomes soft afterward, and the hairs prick the eye, then reapply the medicine to the area of softened skin properly, as you did before; then treat it until it is healed; and that is the form of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that human eyes vary in size and smallness, and according to this, let your constraints be; and the correct path is not easily found by someone who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula, as we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not work, then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap; and let the attendant hold the head between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then place cotton soaked in egg white or juice of parsley over the eye; then heat the cautery which is shaped like: and is pointed at the top like the shape of a dove's feather, this is the cautery; if you wish, it may be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, it may be like a tent; but, this pointed one is better suited for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, open it, and remove the matter; then apply the hot cautery firmly, and hold your hand on the cautery near the part above the eye, so that your hand does not cause harm; and place the cautery on the fatty part of the eye, and destroy it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the bone with the cautery, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then repeat the cautery once more, and again if necessary, and leave it for three days; then apply cotton soaked in butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it is healed; and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, apply an acrid corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat it according to what is written in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that some of the ancients described.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and make a cut; then put into the incision one fine strip of material of which the shape is:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it is made to the size of a lead coin; and hold your hand or the strip firmly, and let the patient not move at all, lest the molten lead run into their eye; and it is necessary that you put over the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white or water.  The lead will burn the fistula area and heal it with marvelous speed.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have described, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a puncture to the nose, and to bring the fistula back to the nose's body according to what is appropriate into its own place.
des crevaices en levres	of the cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often cracks appear in the lips, called "poil," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in the divisions, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small knife-cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly into those cracks until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, treat the area with a plaster until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the uvula, or the palate, or to the roots of the teeth, after it causes decay, rot, and becomes aged and a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; then you insert it into the opening or puncture of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and the innermost part; and do this one or two times, then treat it with what we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is healed thus, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines, and this is of no value, then place the head of the patient in your healthy position; then heat the cautery, of which the form will be shown afterwards in this manner, that you place a rod over the tooth; and quickly place the hot cautery inside, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and repeat the cautery according to your will; then have the patient fill their mouth with salty water, and hold it for an hour and rinse it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth that was moving is strengthened, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupt moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, whether there is cold or a true cold, and the treatments with medicine are of no use, then there is need for cautery in two ways: cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is such that you take cow's butter, and put it on the end of an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and soak it in boiling butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools; and thus do it often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, soak wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron so that the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery with fire is such that you take an iron or bronze cautery, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the sick person; then heat the cautery, in which the form will appear afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the sick person fill their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make cautery of whatever head you wish, and according to your power; and this is the form of the cautery:
des scrophules	of the scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of phlegm and cold moistures, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery, the form of which comes after, and have two openings for the fumes to escape from the other side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and place moistened cotton in butter until the burn is gone; then treat the area with ointments and poultices until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures overcome the channels of the lungs, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be purged by solutive medicines; afterward, you make cautery at the root of the throat, and take care that you do not reach down to the throat itself, and do not burn the heart but slightly.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, make another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cautery, called "clavile," be of the form we have shown previously; and treat the area as we have previously stated until it is healed.
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When coughs and lung illnesses are from cold moistures, and the patient has no fever nor dryness, and the illness is long-standing, then make two cauteries on the ribs in empty spaces; and one other cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cauteries be called "clavile" according to the form previously stated.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you wish, make cautery by pricking with the entire cautery called "points," of which the form is shown previously in the illness of the ears; and let the points be up to thirty, or as many as needed.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, treat the area according to what has been previously stated, and let the cauteries be in three rows according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because of this, the cauteries are lighter, because you make three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, let the patient lie on their back and on their side; then lift the heart that is within the tilth with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, then heat the cautery that has two nerves, of which this is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces right through the side, and the figure of the cautery would be together with four cauteries; and because of this, a cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, so that the figure of the cauterization is six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the thinness of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes one more nerve is added, so that there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, place the cautery on it, to be pressed with a bandage; then make the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, which rarely happens, then apply cautery to the thick part of the clavicle cautery, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is repaired, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is cured.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture enter the stomach, such that they alter it from its complexion, and catarrh multiplies within it, and the customary cures are ineffective, then the patient must be laid on their back, and stretch their legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Thereafter, apply three cauteries: one beneath the breastbone, the size of a finger; one across the entire clavicle; and two outside the two ribs, such that the shape of the cauteries forms a three-angled figure, and there is a spacing between each so that they do not touch when pus forms; and the cauteries should be deep enough to reach both sides of the heart, and the shape of the cauteries should be in this form without any adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and whoever fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and mark the stomach with pricks according to the quantity you desire; then cauterize with the cautery called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have previously described, until he is cured.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver suffers pain from cold, moisture, and large winds, such that it is forced out of its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated as we have described in the sections, and it does not benefit him, then the patient must be laid on their back; and mark three cauteries according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the ribs of the person meet; and have a space of a finger's breadth between each cautery; and let the cauteries be the length of the body; and do not press your hand too much on the cautery; and let only half the heart be burned; and let the patient stand upright; and if they cannot, let them lie down, and extend their legs and raise their arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with a scalpel, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn the entire heart, for you would dry the entire body; and that it does not reach the boil, for the heart is very delicate in that area, and you know it to be true.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too severe; and if it is in the membrane, he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment has ceased to work, the patient should be placed on their head; and then mark the spot where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery that is similar to a ray, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cautery until the heart is burned and reaches the surface, so that the inflammation is entirely gone; after the treatment, according to the treatment of sores, until they are healed; and it is not proper that anyone use this cautery except those who have studied medicine for a long time, and through whose hands these illnesses have passed many times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may boldly operate, and yet I think it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	About cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy, one should use cauteries made of aristolochia roots, in this way: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and long as your fingers; and soak it in oil, and heat it in the fire, and cauterize between the armpit and the neck, and two small cauteries a little lower in the part below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping slightly back; and one cautery in the middle of the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the two sides of the breast, outside the cautery between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but do it openly, as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient ones said that some men use a cautery of iron, similar to a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess; and the pain is relieved, as we said about the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this procedure, there is danger that the patient dies immediately, or a fistula develops that cannot be cured.
de la mice	Of the mice.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of mice according to the divisions of treatments we have discussed, and it does not work, then there are three kinds of cauteries that are all good.
