From the incision next to the temple to the second incision; and burn all the flesh that is between the two cuts, all the surface on the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then place the instrument called a "cultellary" in the first cut; it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge toward the flesh, close to the heart, and the blunt edge toward the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to the heart, and then do the same in the middle cut to the other side; and then drain the blood, and compress the area of blood drawn; then place a bandage of old cotton in each cut, and put wet cloths in wine, oil, and vinegar, and watch for any suppurations; and on the third day, loosen the bandage and apply plenty of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other remedies for healing wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some people experience an acute catarrh, and you see their eyes inflamed and small, their vision weakened, and the eyelids burning; and their hair falls out, and their head hurts acutely, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that these materials and this catarrh come from many veins, and the best cure is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to lie on their back, then make a large cut through the forehead, and another large cut in the shape of a large I.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin the cut from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move the mouth; and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the cut and place old cotton and linen bandages; then bandage with cloths soaked in wine and oil, and beware of any suppuration; when the bandages are removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with things that dry up the moisture, to make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster of it; and apply it to these wounds to cause flesh to grow everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Whatever falls into the ears is one of these four things: either grains, or animal matter, or a piece of ore or similar objects like iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas; or flowing things like water and honey and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or some other object falls into the ear that does not adhere to the ear and does not grow within the ear, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distil a little violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with remedies, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often it comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, then administer extraction with subtle forceps, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the forceps, that is good; if not, then administer extraction with a delicate, small-doubled hook; and if it does not jump out with that, then make a copper wire and put the head of the wire into the ear opening firmly, and plug that which is around the wire with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the wire; then pull it out forcefully, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take glue with which birds are caught, and put in it some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump out by all these things that we have said, then hurry to slice the ear before a hot abscess and spasm come, and the manner of the incision is that you first make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, at the fat or dependent place; and let the incision be like a crescent, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and heal it until it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a delicate thin spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with delicate forceps and by sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, the patient should first use sneezing remedies, and stuff the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it leaks out through this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then he takes many stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and warms them a bit in the fire; and let the patient place one in the opening of their ear, and jump up and down on their feet on the other side, and press another stone onto the stone in the ear; and do not cease to do this, stone on stone, until the water comes out completely, and thus it leaks completely; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and the other end hold over fire until the most of the reed is burned; then do the same with other reeds until the water comes out completely, as we have said with the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of vermin, if it is small, like fleas and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms lodged in the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not work, you must look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, extract them with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the instrument with this shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finer end into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then forcefully suck on the entire instrument; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey and come out, stuff around the instrument with cotton as I said for the stone; and if they do not flee as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in killing worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, narrow below with a small hole, and wide above for distilling; and to press the distillation into it, use a well-made bronze instrument for this, and if you wish, take a spoon and wrap cotton around its tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you wish, into the instrument, and place the instrument in the ear; then place the spoon over the cotton and press firmly with your hand until the oil is distilled or delivered into the ear; and the patient will feel it inside, and the distillations should be warmed on a fire before distilling into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults from the stopping of a wound, or from a growth inside the ear, and sometimes these blockages go deep into the ear, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes a small part of the hole is revealed, and one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which goes deep, so that one cannot see it, requires more thorough treatment in several ways, and in the case where one can see it, you should place the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the obstruction, remove it with this instrument, of which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointed in front and behind, completely smooth, so as not to injure the ear; if the obstruction is a growth or a lump in the ear, hold it with delicate tweezers, and cut it gently until the growth is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is deep within the ear, take a delicate, light scraper, and warm it slightly in the fire, then place it in the ear cavity.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction, from which the patient suffers pain when hearing, pierce it gently, and be careful not to injure the ear's nerves; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose water and sprinkle with crushed vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, you must remove the tent and place another moistened in a cerate made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if blood flows, dip a sponge and bandages in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments to stop the blood flow, which are used to treat discharges.
de la char des papieres	of the skin of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This affliction that comes to the papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and cut it with a spatula from its roots; then put crushed vitriol on the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood flows, cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and the cauterization after the incision is worthwhile; and many times they return, since some thing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there come to the papers of the eyes things that resemble hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "grandine," and is a collection of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the work is such: watch if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and it is an easy thing to know; then open it widely, then lightly scrape it from each part, then take it with tweezers and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the paper a little, do no harm to the patient; and if the fissure is large, assemble it with a stitch, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will restore it soon and produce flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending into the inner ear towards the upper part, turn the paper over, and take the grandine with tweezers, and cut and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is loosened by the incision, this does no harm; and when the grandine is cut, wash the eye with salt water, and treat the place with that which produces flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is formed in webs on the eye papers above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it causes much pain to their eyes, and the runny nose comes in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because tears are constantly flowing from their eyes; and therefore they often lie on their faces, and sleep on their backs, and their eye papers beneath their eyebrows are wet, because the swelling and appearance are covered by the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient should put their head in your lap; then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle, according to the amount of exinach in each part, and put it over it; and press with your fingers on either side, so that the exinach is gathered in the circle; then cut a slit in the middle of the moisture, in the space, with a sharp blade, and it should not be any larger than the incision made in opening a vein; and cut the skin deep until you reach the exinach; and in several places the exinach comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it completely with a piece of cloth held between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to push into the slit, that you do not reach all the way to the eye, that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the slit, then slightly enlarge the slit until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and apply to the area, and bandage it.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some people who grind herbs and apply them to corrupt the remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there comes a hot abscess to the area, treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the eyelids in addition to the natural ones, and they are old, they harm the eyes, and cause various illnesses such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and albuginea, to the point where it causes destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery combined with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before or in the chapter on cautery, or it is done by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head on your chest, then turn the eyelid to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, then place a needle with a thread on top of it; and it should be next to the margin of the eyelid where the hairs grow beside those hairs, and pull the thread on top of the whole eyelid, and turn it towards the blade; then cut in the part underneath the eyelid, underneath the extra hairs, across the whole area, from the large tear duct to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the eyelid, then place on the eyelid a shaped bandage, like a myrtle leaf, and however, the shape must be according to the amount you want to raise the eyelid that is divided into parts.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if someone needs a large amount of the eyelid cut, according to how softened the eyelid is; then cut across the whole area on the two lines that you have marked, starting from the large tear duct to the small one; and one of the cuts should be close to the natural hairs, the width of a hair; then place the forceps in one of the two angles of the wound, then scrape the whole area; then bring the two edges together with stitches from a needle and thin wool thread, wipe the blood, and dry the excess threads on the two eyebrows with some sticky substance, if you wish to do this; and if not, then don't bother; then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitches with drying and constricting things, for the eyelid revives at the healing of the wound and its joining, but stitches are slower (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear; and there is another way: and it is that you mark the eyelid with a shape that is like a myrtle leaf, as we have described, with three separated incisions according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small equal forces, following the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing isn't even, then take a needle with a thread, and place it in the middle of the shape; and put another thread next to the large tear duct, and the second thread next to the small one, and bring the threads together between your fingers evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above where you have marked, as we have described, then bring the two edges of the wound together with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelid are turned: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitches in one and the other are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment for the stitches is according to this form:  and it is that you turn the eyelid and cut into it as I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two thin threads as long as the eyelid and the width of the area is; and cut at the two ends where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly on what is above the eyelid, and firmly hold the two stitches from both sides; and leave it like this for some days, and the skin that is tight will die, and become stiff and rotten, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes time, then cut it with some force, and treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the eyelid is raised, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the two stitches that you will make according to this figure, and according to this amount of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle and put a soft, fine silk thread on it; then bring the ends together and tie them subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then, in a small container, put another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread; then the patient should place their head on your safe surface; and place it near the sun so that the work is clear, because it is a delicate and precise work; then put the needle with the whole container into the root of the hair, and pierce the eyelid quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then pull the hair out over the container, and place in the container any hair there, whether one, two, three, or more; then withdraw your hand until the hair comes out of the entire container into the eyelid with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the container is pulled, and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the container underneath all the thread you have placed on it, until the container comes out through the hole above, and you see it through the eye's vision; then you pull the container and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and the skin grows over; and if the hair is small, then attach a long hair from the natural eyebrows and lift it up with that or leave it there until it lengthens and then lift it up.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati," or rot, comes to the eye, there are two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs through the wounding of a cut or a cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment is to split the wound, separate its edges, and place linen strips inside, and bind it until it is healed; and you should not use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and irrigate it with water or boiled flaxseed and melted diachylon ointments in any of the oils, and wrap it in a bandage, and treat it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the key to your treatment is to ensure that it does not heal in the same way as before; and these treatments that we have mentioned are only to prevent the disease from returning in the same way as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is beneath, which is truly called "axacrati," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental form comes from wounds, cuts, cautery, and similar things; and the method of treatment is to take a needle with a double thread, and pierce the flesh, starting from the left tear duct and going to the right, so that the thread comes out at two points in the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the needle and cut it with a spatula wide enough.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the membrane returns as it should, that's good; if not, take a scraper and place it in the fissure, turn the membrane, and make two cuts along the sides of the membrane; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision you made, and form an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "I Greek"; then remove the flesh, according to the amount its edges are sharpened underneath, from what was next to the membrane, then join the two separated parts and stitch them with a woolen thread; then treat it with the softening medicines and compresses that we have described, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a cut, stitch, or cautery, you must make a straight cut beneath the hairs of the membranes, as previously described; then separate between the two edges with a compress, as I said; and the work must be done according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the skilled masters apply all their ingenuity to make the shape return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what work and instruments are needed in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	Sudden tearing of the membrane
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this adhesion occurs in a person in such a way that the membrane above is glued to the white of the eye and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must place the tip of a scraper under the membrane and lift it upward; and stretch it with forceps, until you cut what is in excess with a fine spatula, which should not be too sharp or too pointed, so that the patient cannot bear the sharp spatula injuring the eye; and make your incision, with which you peel off that adhesion, gently, so that the membrane returns to its natural shape; and the entire adhesion is healed, and sometimes a saline solution is placed in the eye, followed by a rinse with fresh water and a poultice; then place a linen compress between the membrane and the eye, and apply wet wool soaked in egg white to the eye; and after three days use poultices and softening substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two types: one is fibrous and resembles a hard surface, and another that is not fibrous, but resembles frozen white moisture, which, when touched with iron and attempted to be pulled with forceps, cannot be done; and both types begin near the large tear duct, and grow gradually until they cover the entire vision and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the incision is that the patient should place their head in your lap, then open their eyes; and you lift the membrane with your hand, then grasp the nail with small forceps and extend it upward; then take a needle and thread it with a horsehair, or cowhair, or oxhair, and a strong thread; and slightly double the point of the needle and insert it into the nail, piercing it completely; and tie the nail with the thread and extend it upward, and scrape with the hair the side of the nail that adheres to the pupil and the eyelid down to the root; then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct using a fine spatula and gentle pressure, leaving the natural tear duct tissue, so that the flow of tears is not disturbed by the incision; and sometimes the nail can be treated with tweezers alone and thread, as we have said; then it is scraped away with a gentle spatula in the manner described:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch or break the fleshy tissue and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision, apply a small amount of crushed lead and a poultice made of litharge to the eye, and leave it until the following day; then treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not fibrous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the tweezers cannot grasp it, this type of nail condition is often treated with medicines; and it grows as described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, open the patient's eye and take a slightly pointed spatula in this manner:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully scrape the nail away; and if you see that it decreases and the edges approach, then apply a poultice made of litharge, red ointment, and crushed lead to the eye from your mouth, and cover the eye until the next day; then continue this procedure until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is any condition contrary to this in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then drain it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the procedure as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the tear duct tissue harms the eye greatly, then hold it with tweezers, and cut off a portion, but not all of it, so that the flow of tears is not interrupted; then apply red ointment made of litharge to the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Sometimes red flesh grows in the eyes of some men, covering the pupil and pressing against the eyelids, and resembling a rose of ballasts.  The procedure is for the patient to place their head in your lap, then open their eyes, and use suitable tweezers to grasp all the flesh and hold it firmly. Then cut off the initial flesh and continue to shave away until it is all removed. Be careful not to injure the eye during the procedure.  The incision should be similar to the incision described earlier for removing nails, using gentle force to remove the impurities, as demonstrated in the following section of this chapter. Once the incision is complete and all flesh removed, apply crushed lead or red ointment and similar corrosive medicines to the eye. Place a bandage of egg white over the eye to prevent the formation of a hot abscess. If anything remains and a hot abscess threatens to form, leave the eye and treat the abscess with remedies for a hot abscess, and then return to the procedure once it heals. Treat any similar growths that appear on the eye in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you should always consider the treatment for each eye, addressing both its natural and accidental conditions, using iron tools for the latter.  Never put your hand to work on either eye until you determine that the limb will tolerate the procedure.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins covering the eye impair its function and weaken the eye over time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first examine the eye to see if the redness is simply an affliction and no other illness is present.  If so, proceed as follows: instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, and then carefully grasp those veins with tweezers, the tweezers being thin and double in the manner shown.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let the two tweezers be positioned in a row in one piece following this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gently grasp the veins, and wipe away the blood one moment after another until you see the affected veins removed from the eye.  Be careful not to damage the eye with the tips of the tweezers, and perform this procedure at midday in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you only cut the veins.  After you have done this, instill green and red colored liquid into the eye to eliminate any remaining redness.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot remove it all at that time, apply a soothing eye plaster and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and you are certain of the absence of any hot abscess.  Then, begin again according to the aforementioned method until it is healed. And this is the method of application:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is known as an "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously described, and it is not healed, then you must cut into the abscess, wherever it needs to be opened, and remove all the moisture within, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, clean it with all the instruments that this method provides; and it is called an "aspre chief," and is made of iron, sharpened at one end, and pointed like a file, as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the corrupt bone, then rotate it between your fingers and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the area is healed, and flesh grows, and the body of the boil is healed, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not regenerate or become an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, there is no other method than to return the fistula to the opening of the nose, according to this form: and that you expose the bone a second time with iron and sharp medicines, and when it is exposed, you take a drill according to this form, and let the iron tip be sharpened at three angles, and the shaft be tapered to a point as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the entire drill until it pierces the bone, and the patient will feel it by the wind escaping if they hold their hand over their nose; and then restore the area with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the area hardens, the matter goes to the nose; this is a more manageable situation for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the eye's discharge
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is completely open and there is no disturbance to the nose or decrease, you must bandage the patient.  Then, heal it, then apply cupping glasses or leeches without pricking to draw out the matter. Then place on the eye a compress made of asafoetida, aloe, frankincense, and gum tragacanth, and then compress the eye, and place the plaster over it with bandages and strips. The method of the strips is to take fairly soft strips, and double each into four, and then place one over the other according to the size the eye requires; then compress it tightly over a stiff bandage, and repeat the cupping to draw out the matter without pricking; then remove the cupping glasses and keep the eye compressed day and night, and if the bandage loosens, you must compress it tightly.  Then remove the compress after a day and night.  If you see the eye improving, that is good; otherwise, repeat the plaster, strips, compress, and cupping until healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the tearing of a cloth or garment.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear occurs in the cloth or garment, and it opens, and appears as if it contains small resin granules, and is frightening to see; then, if you see it has to be cut, the work is such that you place a needle at the root of the damaged part, down to the top, then place another needle where there is a double thread from the tear.  Pierce it, and leave the first needle according to the layout.  Then cut the double thread and tie a part of the fabric around it, and compress it well, then pull out the needle and place a wool covering, soaked in egg white, on the area; and leave it until the thread comes loose with the cloth, then treat the area with healing things until the wound is healed.  And sometimes the wound is restrained by the fabric, with a cloth bandage, around it, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows a significant appearance, then pierce it with a very thin lancet that goes deep into the eye, and drain the white moisture and lower the eye, and immediately put it back in place; then treat it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the swelling of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness, called "alcunnati," is nothing more than a swelling in the eye, resembling a drop descending, but it is not actually fluid.  The method of treatment is to have the patient sit on a proper and straight chair, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it so that you see the swelling come to the level of your eyes.  Then it should be kept in place, and not descend, and the light should be unobstructed, and the patient should be able to see things as before.  And if it does not descend, know that it is an infection, and if the swelling does not move as described.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then have the patient sit in your hands, then take a thin lancet and pierce the cornea slightly along the juncture of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, so that the swelling comes out.  And when it is out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or water with fenugreek boiled in it and honey, into the eye, then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Of the inflammations of the eye.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have already described the types of inflammations in the divisions, and what is required for piercing;  treat according to the severity.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should have the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and cover the healthy eye firmly. Then put the affected eye on your left hand if it is the left eye, or on your right hand if it is the right eye; then, in your right hand if it is the left eye, or in your left hand if it is the right eye, take the instrument called "almagda"; then place the point of the instrument beside the crown, the thickness of a finger, in the white part of the eye, near the tear duct, then insert the "almagda" instrument carefully, and move your hand so that it pierces the white part of the eye until you feel the instrument reach the empty space, and the length of the "almagda" should be from the pupil to the end of the black part; and that is the crown of the eye, you will see the bone in that membrane because of the clarity of the cornea, and then place the instrument into where the inflammation is, and then express the matter out one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the inflammation descends now, the patient sees before him, and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, if the inflammation rises again, press with the instrument, and when it is firmly placed and does not rise, gently withdraw the almagda by turning your hand little by little.  Then add a little gem salve to the inflammation, and remove that from the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a bandage of wool or cloth soaked in rose oil and egg white to the affected eye, and cover it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply a common bandage with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are some people whose eyes are too hard, you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle opening, then insert the almagda, as we have said.  And for the completion of the work, prepare a comfortable bed for the patient, where they sleep on their back in a dark place; and be free from all movement, and let them eat light foods, and do not move their head to the right or left, and keep them bandaged according to their disposition for three days. Then unbandage them in the same dark room, and test their vision, and show them some objects, and then reapply the bandage until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the time of the treatment or after the incision immediately, but you must delay this, because the inflammation rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If a painful abscess develops, unbandage the eye before the seventh day, and apply what soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, unbandage the eye and place a bandage over it for a few days, and keep them in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then gradually leave the room, and return to their life; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us from the East, who told us that in their country, people made a device to pierce the almagda, with which one sucks out the fluid, but nevertheless, I have never seen one in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the shapes of the almagda, so that those who do not know them may see; and they are properly of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And their head should be of the same fineness, and the tail in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes various additional flesh grows on the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many legs; and there are some in which there is a sunken flesh of a dark color, and there is soft flesh of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the soft flesh, not sunken, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open their nostrils, and apply a lancet to that flesh, and draw it out; then cut what you can remove with a thin sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that cannot be cut, you should remove it with all the thin instruments gently, so that nothing remains; and if it is without pus, or a hot abscess, treat it as appropriate; and if it is a malignant abscess, you must hurry and cauterize it until the pus is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then apply an easy and sharp incision on the nose, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose opens, and pus comes down to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the pus does not come out as it should, know that there is flesh growing on the bone above, which the instrument cannot reach to cut: then you must tie a slightly thick linen thread with your hands, and place a space of one or less inch between each knot; and make the patient place the end of the thread in his nose with all his power, and pull it while smelling, until it comes out from the nose into the mouth; and children often do this at school, and it is an easy thing for whoever wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and draw one after the other, while holding the knots that are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have decayed that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then put a lead wire in the nose for a few days until it is healed, and if drying medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for cleansing the nose, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or bronze, similar to an open lamp, like a wire, and the conduit also; and if you wish, make a closed wire, and let the instrument be full to cleanse the nose; and let it have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a sickness called "telul" arises at the top of the nose, and grows and becomes large often, until it is a visible thing to look at; and therefore you should cut it at the beginning, and remove it completely, then apply the cautery or burning medicine to the spot; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, take heed if it is hard, of a dark color, and lacking sensation: do not touch it with iron, for it is a festering abscess, because when cut sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not dark in color, and you see that it can be completely cut, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to someone, examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two edges with a stitch, and treat it until it is healed; and if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, then you should cauterize all the parts of their edges until they bleed, then join the two edges with a stitch, and tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood and powdered frankincense; and put a piece of strong or other uniting plaster over the powders, and leave it until it dries naturally, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	Abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.
