In some people, hard abscesses occur inside the lips, resembling grains of millet, both small and large; then you must turn back the lips, and cut open each one, and remove it with forceps and cut it away in each part; then fill the space after the incision with powdered vitriol, until the bleeding is stopped; and then remove excess, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, extra flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; you should grasp it with forceps and cut it at its root, allowing the pus or blood to drain; then apply powdered vitriol, or other astringent and drying powders, to the area.  If this flesh returns after the first incision, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: it will not return after the cauterization.  And these are the methods of using instruments to make the cuts.
des sordens	Of the sordens (or, possibly, sores)
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, hard, rough scabs gather at the base of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums.  Sometimes the teeth become dark, yellow, or spotted with decay, and the gums become foul-smelling.  You should position the patient between your hands, their head in your grasp, and scrape away the scabs and any discoloration that you see, until no more remains.  Treat the dark spots, greenish discolorations, yellowing, and other blemishes in this way until they are gone.  If the first scraping removes the problem, well and good.  Otherwise, repeat the procedure on the second and third days until it is all removed.  Note that teeth require different types of scraping tools, as demonstrated by the craftsman, because the scrapers used for general tooth cleaning are different from those used for cleaning between the teeth.  Be prepared with these and other appropriate tools.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating a toothache, you should delay extracting it as long as possible, for this should not be done unless there is a clear need to remove it.  For it is a very delicate substance until that point, so there should be no need to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient must have the tooth extracted, you must be certain of the afflicted tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often, the pain deceives the patient, and they believe it is in a healthy tooth and have a good tooth extracted; however, the pain does not disappear because of this, and the bad tooth remains. We ourselves have seen this happen with the nobility.  When you are sure of the aching tooth, you must scrape around it thoroughly with a strong instrument to protect the gum on all sides. Then, gently and gradually use your fingers or fine pliers to carefully loosen the tooth until it is well detached, then firmly grasp the pliers.  Hold the patient's head firmly between your knees, holding it steady so it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Then extract the tooth straight, without breaking it. If it does not readily come out, use one of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is decayed and hollow, you must fill it with strips of cloth where the cavity is, and gently extract it with pliers so it does not break when you pull.  And you must work carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it off and leave a piece behind, as a larger, more painful part of the root will remain in the patient, causing more pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be wary of doing as ignorant practitioners do, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the jaw, and do not achieve what we have described. Instead, they sometimes cause more serious illness from the remaining roots or from breaking the jaw, as we have often observed. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine, vinegar, or oil. If bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol. If this is not effective, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one first moves the teeth, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth out.  And these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have large, sturdy limbs so that they do not bend when pulling, and should be made of good, strong iron, and have teeth for holding the teeth.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, you must place cotton soaked in butter on the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area softens, then apply the pliers called "algefri," which the head resembles the beak of a bird; and the insides should be shaped like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with these pliers, you must expose the flesh all around the root and apply the instrument called "althali," that is to say, a scraper, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out with this, it is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which the forms come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the proportion of the teeth, and this instrument that resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And these instruments should be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many instruments for the teeth are available; and also other instruments, which are not listed; and the wise and skillful master will find his instrument himself, according to his works and the patient's condition, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of others; and if one breaks the cart or other bones, or where it might, then look for the appropriate instruments that I have told you, and use the gestures of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with suitable remedies for this, and if there is a small rot in the bone, remove it with all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body form, and the shape is ugly, especially in young women, you must know if the tooth was born after the other tooth, and is not in the right place, and it cannot be filed nor smoothed; then remove it; and if it is close to the tooth, take this instrument, of which this is the form, and it resembles a small beak, and it is made of sharp, hard iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And remove it bit by bit over several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, file it with a file like this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth little by little over several days gently, so that it does not move until it is removed; then smooth it with any scraper at the end, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen, either from a blow or falling, and the patient cannot bite without them falling out, and you have treated them with binding medicines, and this is no use; then you must bind them with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and put it double between two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you carefully reach the other healthy tooth; then repeat the covering until the part where you started, and gently and skillfully tighten your hand, so that it does not move; and make your binding at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, join them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and position it so that it does not injure the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, bind it with another thread; so it will remain and serve thus for all its time, and this is the method for the teeth and the method for straightening two healthy teeth, and two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is repositioned in its place, little by little, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes a tooth shape is made from cow bone, and it is placed in the place where the gap is, and it is bound as we have said, and remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of cutting the tongue ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament that comes under the tongue is natural, and one is born with it; or by accident from a stitched wound; and the method is that you open the patient's mouth, and hold their head steady, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament from the side, so that the tongue is separated from its hold; and if there is hardness or scar tissue, from the stitching of a wound, insert a hook and cut the ligament from the side; and take care that the cut is not too deep, because of the artery underneath; and when you have done it, wash the area with rose water and oil, or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and the patient should keep this in place every night so the wound cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place powdered vitriol on the area; and if the bleeding is excessive, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a dark or black or hard discoloration, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is tending toward a whitish color, and there is moisture, insert a hook, and slice it with a thin spatula, and remove it from both sides; and if the bleeding is excessive during your work, apply powdered vitriol until it stops, then return to your work until you have cleared everything; then wash the area with oil and vinegar, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are bumps in the throat called "godath," properly called the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we said in the division, and they do not heal, take care: if they are hard abscesses of small size and dark color, do not touch them with an iron tool.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but let it ripen, and then you will open it, or it will break open on its own; and if it is whitish, pale in color, and the root is small, prepare the instrument for cutting, but first check if the abscess is warm and has subsided.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, with their head in your lap, and let the patient open their mouth, and let the surgeon take the tongue between their hands, and press the tongue underneath with the entire instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine bronze, like a small knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the lancet and insert it into the tonsil, and draw it firmly upwards as far as you can; and draw some matter out with it, then cut it with the instrument, whose form is like a pair of forceps; and however, the ends are bent, and one end against the other, and are very sharp, and are made from iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, cut it with pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let one side be sharp, and the other not; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, let the patient gargle with hot water, and lukewarm water, and if bleeding occurs, let the patient gargle with water, or with cooked pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped; then treat it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut these likewise as the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed in her throat, specifically a small abscess; and it had nearly completely closed the throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had swollen so much that it had forced out two nostrils through the two nasal openings.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a lancet into one, then pulled out a large portion of pus; then I did the same in the other nasal opening, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterward I inserted the lancet into the abscess, and cut a portion, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into the abscess for a long time; and the abscess would repeatedly grow back and fill the space I had emptied, until it became quite large; then I cauterized it in the throat; thus it stopped growing; and I left the area, and do not know what God did to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When mucus flows down to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment is not effective, and you see that the inflamed abscess is subsiding, and it is small, then you should cut it open; and the one that is round, gathered, and not elongated; and it is bloody or of a dark color or black, you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have described, its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument we previously mentioned; then, insert the hook into the eye, pull it downwards, and cut it open with one of the two instruments I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you should only cut away the excess that is beyond the natural boundary; for if you cut more, you will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of the cut, you should use a device for cauterization to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp, sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head in your lap, then press their tongue against the instrument we mentioned in the cautery chapter, and cauterize with a hot, sharp iron, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and fill the tip of this instrument, whose shape is as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there should be a small receptacle on the head, where medicine is placed, like the bowl of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the sore; and the patient should lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down into the throat and harm it; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the sore for about half an hour, until you see it is healed and the medicine's burn has subsided; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and dip the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with the cotton over the sore, so that the cotton sticks to the sore; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four or five days. And if you need to reapply the cautery medicine, reapply it, and after the cautery, wipe around the sore with cotton soaked in butter, and clean anything around the medicine; and let it be washed with cold water, and treated with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is more effective than incision, or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamint and ysop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avron and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and put water in it, and let it boil; and the pot should be well sealed from strong earth, and inside the pot there should be an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or brass, and one of the ends should be put into the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the sore through the opening, until the sore is deadened; after that, repeat often until the sore dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, because many things can happen; and do not do this except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a tube and put the end of it into a cracked egg, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; because the cracked egg prevents the vapor from irritating the mouth, and this is a good and safe treatment overall.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times bone or fish spines, or some other object, lodge in the throat; therefore, you should pull out anything you can see, and press the tongue towards the sun with the instrument, so you can see the object move; and for what you do not see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the object will be expelled by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the location, it will stick, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out with the methods we have described, take a lead instrument in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so it can more easily enter the throat, and have the patient's head raised; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that no harm comes to it, and do not push the bone deeper; it is better if the patient pushes the instrument, so that it moves to where the object is lodged; if it goes down, pull it out with the instrument evenly, until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the leech in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the leech is treated, as I have said in the division, through medicine; and when that is not helpful, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, and press the tongue with the instrument I have described to you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, pull it out with a small hook, or with fine pliers suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, take a hooked chain, and put it in the patient's throat, then put a hot iron onto the hook of the chain, and do this repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is feverish all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with the hand repeatedly; and as soon as the leech feels the water, it falls off.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall off as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall off without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are glowing coals, and the bottom is covered with a pierced lid, and through this hole is the end of the instrument; then pour your fumigation in, and the patient places the hook of the chain in their mouth, and closes the mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but goes down to the leech; and the leech will fall off now, and if it does not fall off, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient will suffer thirst, and eat salty and dry things, and drink no water; and it will then be necessary for it to come off by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one pulls the leech, if one can see it, is like curved pliers to allow the mouth to enter the throat; and it resembles the beak of a bird of prey, and there is roughness from a file, so that once it has taken hold, it cannot let go; and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses exist, according to what is remembered here from others in this book, and they are diverse in their perforation and incision; and there are two types, one in its own appearance, and from the moisture it contains.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second type is according to the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of the fleshy areas are different from those that develop in joints, and each requires its own judgment in treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is ripe according to its maturation; and there are some that must be pierced when they are swollen and do not ripen according to their maturation, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess develops near a joint, and it is left to fester, it may corrupt the ligaments and nerves of the joint, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near a major limb, if you delay the perforation until it ripens, it will harm the main limb; if it is near the foundation, it is pierced sooner than it is ripe; and you should not pierce a swollen abscess without complete digestion, except for the one near the foundation, lest it fester deeply, extend inward, and become a fistula, unable to heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for perforating a ripe abscess, according to its completion, when the pain subsides, and the fever recedes, and the lessening of pain and redness, and the quieting of the abscess head, and the other signs; and you must make the perforation at the most dependent part of the abscess, where it appears to move; and let the perforation be along the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and in all such places, equally, where there is no membrane.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy area, it is better that you delay the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before then, the poison will spread throughout, and it is full of foul matter; and perhaps the edges will harden and deepen.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if some abscesses are pierced according to the width of the body, according to the needs of the member.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary to make small openings in small abscesses; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and there are abscesses where it is necessary to cut the core, and to cut; when it has become like a flap, and is inactive, it is necessary to do as is done with boils; and there are some that are split into three angles, and some that are cut like a myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the groin; and there are some where a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those that do not have a head, like superficial soft abscesses, it is necessary to pierce them fully; and when the abscess is large, and it has gathered a large boil, and you pierce it, do not remove all the boil at once, but remove a portion; then close the abscess until the next day, and then remove some more; do this repeatedly, gradually, until all the boil is removed; especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or young children, or decrepit old men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes trembles with the discharge of the boil, so that the patient may die, and you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, clean the wound, and see if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a simple incision, apply flax or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you place a bandage in each one so that they meet; and if you have cut a portion of skin in the abscess and you have cut around it, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or linen scraps without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if a flow of blood occurs in your work, apply cool and easy water, and wet a cloth, and apply it repeatedly to the bleeding area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and remedies, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book in the relevant locations.  And if it is during winter, and the area where the abscess is is very sensitive, it is necessary to apply bandages and cloths soaked in wine and warm oil; and if it is during summer, and the area is fleshy, it is necessary that you place cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cool oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess, clean it, and treat it as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head's interior comes small abscesses, and there are varieties of them that are like webs,  like the yolk of an egg, and many of them are similar.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are greasy and some where there is moisture, like pus; and there are some which are hard and stony when cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not resist.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the incision is that you use any instrument that is called "entromissoire," of which the form is shown below, and what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cut through it from above along the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then cauterize without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it returns often when you leave anything; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; and that will heal what remained from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for it until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess has a thick fat, cut it along this shape, lengthwise; and throw your incisions, and cauterize it from all sides, and apply all your treatment to draw the pus out of the part where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do what I have said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same with an abscess if it is stony, and in cutting and treating it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting on a stony and moist abscess is easier, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses are in the head where there is no moisture, and such was the abscess that I cut in the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck it, one would have made as much of a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come to the head, except those which come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place, in order to let the pus exit; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	of the scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses appear on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and are joined together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous swelling is properly within its own skin, like the pus and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the forms of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that will not yield to healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one, then, which you see of good disposition when touched, and is the same color as the body, and moves freely on every side and is not attached to the nerves of the neck, nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not deep; you should cut it from above, and scrape it off from every part, and spread the two flaps of the skin with forceps, if you need to, as we said for head abscesses; and drain it slowly, and be certain not to cut the nerve or the vein, and let the instrument not be sharp or cutting, lest the hand slip, and do not go too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and that prevents you from working, then put powdered vitriol in the wound, or some powders that stop the blood, and tighten the wound; and leave it until the abscess has subsided, and the wound has softened, and begun to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood has stopped, return to your work until you complete it; then, use your index finger to see if there remain any small swellings, and cut and drain them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the swelling, you should not cut that swelling at its root, but tie it off with a strong double thread, and let it fall off, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire swelling, you should join the two edges of the wound, and stitch it now, since no excess remains due to the size of the swelling.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	You must then attend to cutting the root of it, and pulling it out, and stitching it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those swellings that hold excess, pierce where it appears ripe; and pierce it as the previously mentioned one, dependently, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it consumes what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with ointment that generates flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of quinsey
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of throat-cutting; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with quinsey, it is necessary that the throat fissure called "epiglottis" be relieved; and that no help be given by this, because all the veins and the body fluids of the sick are with those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the lungs, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below three or four small transverse incisions, between the two circles or by the amount of the incision's surface, not in the cartilage; and that place is so suitable for the epiglottis' section that there is no flesh there, and the vessels are far away.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, he must stretch the skin of the throat to the whole opening, then cut the membrane until it reaches the channel; and drain the blood vessels if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm that jumps out through the broken place, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed in which one fears strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound in the membrane, and stitch it together without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely closed, and the patient is judged to be dying, and breathing is failing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then the epiglottis is cut so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to stitch the wound and heal it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young woman take a knife and stick it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and also that she had not cut any vein or conduit other than the throat, and the breath was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed it until it was sound; and the young woman suffered nothing more than a sore throat, and returned to her normal condition; for this reason, I say that there is no need to fear cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and is a large abscess, the color of a jaundice, and is common in women; and it is according to two types: natural and accidental; in the natural type, there is no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type is in two ways, of which one is like fat tumors, and the other type is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is cause for fear, and it is not necessary to operate with strong measures except in those that are small, and probe and search throughout the interior: if you find it like a fat tumor, and it is not connected to any vein, then cut it, as one cuts tumors, and remove it with all its covering, if any; and search well all around, and treat it as necessary until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many kinds of tumors are there, of which I will describe all the appearances; and now it is necessary that I state the whole difference between a tumor and an issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue has heat and fever until the boiling is passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	A tumor has neither heat, nor fever, nor pain, and contains a sac, which is its own pouch, and is the same color as the body, and begins like a blister and grows larger; and there are two types, either fatty or moist, and many colors as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treating a tumor, that you first examine it with all the instruments called "entromissoires", according to the form it takes in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to examine abscesses of tumors is that you should take the moistest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, as appropriate to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the instrument, and be careful lest anything should jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the running moisture flows, whatever color it may be, then lance it as I have described for other abscesses; and if, after the instrument, no moisture comes, know that it is fatty, so lance it then in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape it from each side, and watch the skin where it lies, so that you pull it away healthy with the tumor; and if you cannot pull it away healthy, then pull it away in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains, the tumor will return many times; and if a little remains, and the blood bothers you, then fill the wound with some sharp, corrosive powders, and constrict the wound, and put on soothing hot poultices, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the tumor is large, stitch the two edges of the wound, and treat it with those things that create flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if a throbbing vein is contrary to you, or another thing, hurry and fill the place with pulverized vitriol, and leave it for two or three days, so that the wound becomes rotten and the boiling of the blood subsides; then return to cauterizing what remains of the tumor.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments for probing, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to search for abscesses of fistula; and they are like the needles with which one stitches wounds, and they are of yellow bronze, or iron, or silver, and the ones that are yellow are better; and they are tested with black lead for searching for fistulous sores; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the probes are of many appearances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are probes that have two curves of three kinds as well; and there are probes that have three curves, and they are also of three kinds; and there are probes that have two curves, and probes with only one curve, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these, with which one probes, is sharp, and some of them do not cut very much on one side only, with which one scrapes away tumors, so that one does not cut the vein or nerve; and of these probes are the lancets placed in handles, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them much except in fleshy areas, such as legs, arms, breasts, and sores, and in similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the peelings of figs, according to this shape, with which one stops blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the place where there is a cut of veins and arteries, and sometimes in accordance with this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must do it according to this shape from this line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with a medicine that generates flesh, then bring together the two edges of the wound with sutures, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast sags, and is softened due to its size, as happens in women, then cut it into two portions above, with two similar cuts; whereby one is connected to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller, according to this shape, from this line .b. up to line .g.; then scrape off the skin between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sutures and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healthy; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the outflow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the remaining and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas, where there are lumps, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and cure with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofulas, cut it as we have said in the cutting of scrofulas, and if the wound returns pus, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above is closed, there often results an abscess, and this likewise happens to the swollen vein and abscess; and if one recognizes that it is due to the artery, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a tightening; and when it is due to the vein, swelling is apparent; and it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and the angles and the neck and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
