It is necessary then to avoid iron treatment, and what is at the head must also be avoided, and in that which is from swelling of the artery, cut through the skin lengthways; then open the incision with the lancets, and nicely separate the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered; then put a needle under it, and pierce it to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then puncture the place between the two ligatures with a probe until the blood within issues forth, and the abscess is relieved; then apply the treatment that removes pus, until the ligature falls off; then treat with a suitable ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, it is necessary that you hold with your hand what you can of the abscess to the entire skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and let there be a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or the ligature of one of the two sides to the two ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not hold firmly, then reinsert another needle to the entire thread under the entire abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the excess issues forth, then cut away the excess of the heart and leave what is bound; then place a cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply treatments of poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses arise in the artery and in the vein, abscesses arise in the nerves when they are injured, or by excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and the fingers and in all places where there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various positions, causing pain; and when it is squeezed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but under the heart; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, or underneath or above, and that which is in the joints should not be cut with iron; for there might result contraction; and that which is in the head or the forehead, the skin is cut in a straight line.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with pliers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, scrape it with a lancet, and peel it, then remove it and stitch the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and nowhere else, a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and its roots are subtle, and its head is large; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had small roots, and were often cracked, and moisture often flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found eighteen ounces in one, and six in the other, and the work in the incision is that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and with subtle roots; so cut it with a large scalpel, and have the fire cautery present.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting, there are often excessive bleeding, and if the blood overwhelms you, then quickly cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision with the iron, take a well-made lead thread, and tie the tumor with it as we said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the lead thread until it cuts the tumor and it falls off without effort; and if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting, especially for the abdomen, but you can cut the half, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tumor that is of a fixed color and of poor feeling and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a festering abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the swelling is severe
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the swelling appears due to cautery on a wound or a rupture of the skin, and is on the abdomen, and some of the swellings come out, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries, as was stated before, or from wind; and if it is due to a rupture of the skin and the exit of pus, the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and is a slight thing without pain, and shows different exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with one's fingers, it yields and then returns, and perhaps it is closed, and it greatly increases at the entrance to the bath and due to hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and is clearly seen when you press it with your hand, and does not resist; and if it is due to blood, the abscess appears large and hard, and is lodged according to a certain amount; and if it is due to wind, it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery, or a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you should abandon the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, then you must instruct the patient to hold their breath, and be stretched out straight, then mark the area around the sore; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the area you marked with all the spatulas, then extend the half of the abscess above the large incisions; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the stitches be loose; then open the half of the abscess extended over the stitches, and place your index finger in it, and look for the intestine; if you find it caught by the stitches, then untie it, and push the intestine outside the belly; and if you find the bowel, then grasp it with the incisions, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, then go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and place the two needles around what you have made in a cross that you pierced; then compress the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you want, remove the needles, and let the area rot, and the dead flesh fall off by itself; or you cut it when it is softened and rotten, then treat it with what is necessary, and complete the abscess as we have said; and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area with what is necessary, and close the area.
dou chancre	of the sore/ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the types of sores, and how to treat them with medicine, and how to avoid treating them with iron; and we say that the sore begins in the flesh, and great caution is necessary in its treatment. The ancients said that when a sore is in a place where it can be scraped off, like a sore on the breasts, and in the thigh, and similar places, it should be completely removed when it is in its early stages; and when it is large and old, you should not approach it, for I have never cured one, and no one ever cured one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile several times; then make him bleed if he has a noticeable fullness, then prepare a good place for the procedure; then put your incisions on the sore and cut around it on all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and press the area with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding opposes you with the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the types of dropsy, how the accumulation of water occurs, the signs of each type, and the treatment with medicine and with iron:  only in the case of "eclitēs" is it acceptable to use iron;  and you should not use iron in these two types: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because they are fatal.  So, when you treat this type of dropsy called "eclitēs" with medicine, and the treatment is not successful, consider if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as diarrhoea or similar things;  do not use iron, for there is danger. And if you see a strong patient, and they have only dropsy, and are neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed as follows: lift the patient straight into your hands, and the attendant should press the abdomen, pushing the water towards the lower part of the chest;  then take the pointed spatula in this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be sharp on both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And be pointed, and yet not so sharp that it can penetrate to the intestines when inserted and cause injury; then examine if the dropsy is located towards the intestines: in that case, you should make a cut above the rib cage, three fingers directly beneath the incision; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, the cut should be to the left of the rib cage, three fingers; and if it is due to the spleen, it should be to the right, and the patient should not lie on the incision so that the excess fluid does not flow to that weak spot; then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, place it, and lift your hand so that the spatula is between the skin and the surface, as if making a thin incision; then pierce the surface until the spatula reaches the empty space, which is the location of the fluid, then drain it completely; and insert this instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a fine silver chain, and is made of bronze or light metal, and has one small hole on the underside;  and on one side, three holes; and two on another, and one on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision, like a scribe cuts a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the head is the opening, so that when the instrument reaches the fluid, it immediately descends onto the instrument;  then empty it by half or a third, because if you empty more than necessary at that time, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of their vital spirit, or will fall into a coma, or approach death; but drain it according to the patient's strength, and according to the indications of the patient's constitution and their pulse; then remove the instrument and retain the fluid, and it is now retained by the valve that stops the hole in the surface, which you pierced in this manner;  then re-use the instrument the next day if the patient is able, and drain a small amount of fluid; do this for several days, and be careful not to leave any but a small amount of fluid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you are unsure about the patient, and you leave too much fluid, treat them with a hot grave or sand bath, or by sweating or bathing and exposure to the sun, and give them to drink; and treat them with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize over the stomach, liver, and spleen after the fluid has been drained, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born with no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, it should be pierced very subtly in this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place a small lead plug in the opening, and tie it and keep it in place for three or four days. When it wants to urinate, remove the plug, and let it urinate, then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes forth will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose opening is small, should be medicated with a lead plug, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are injured, for some are born with the opening at the top of the penis, so that they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the substance cannot reach the prostate, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the operation is that the patient lies often on their back, then extends the head of the penis and cuts it like the blade of a pen, so that the opening falls in the middle as is necessary; and beware of the bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop it with something that stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Blisters on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils appear on the penis, and it is an unsightly appearance of flesh; and some are malignant, and some are not; therefore you must take them with a fine forceps, and cut and clean them all, then apply moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of foul color and smelling, you must apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the boil is on the surface of the penis, and part is inside the skin and part outside, you must remove the boil that is inside first; and when it is healed, treat the outside one.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, the head of the penis is not secure that it will not be pierced, and blackening and corruption come to the penis and the testicles; you must remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and figs, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a discharge of blood comes, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery aids two conditions together: namely, blood discharge and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupt and retracted, you must insert a lead tube into the penis and allow the patient to urinate; and when the skin is burned on the head of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or if it happens due to a wound or an abscess, you must then cauterize it with a sharp instrument, until the adhesion is broken, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if it is a severe task to separate them, you must cauterize a small portion of the head of the penis and skin with a spatula; then gently separate them and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water between them, so it does not burn again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not simply the separation of a continuation like other wounds; however, when we perform this procedure of our own volition, and especially on children, it is necessary that we perform the best and least painful procedure for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we only know what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most masters and nobles who performed circumcision using a knife, and force, and a single blade; the hearts feared because there are two layers, and perhaps one layer above is cut while the other layer below remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Therefore, it must be cut, and the pain is doubled, and the cleansing that comes with the knife is not certain for the tip of the member; and with the cleansing of the nail, the knife might accidentally miss it, and damage the procedure, and many times they heal without needing cleansing and I have witnessed this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing that is done with force, through the entire thread of the wire, I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the force cuts exactly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts evenly throughout all at once; but let the thread be tight around the skin; and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis, and you can make him happy in every way you can; then, hold it between your hands straight, and place the force between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then, put your hand on the penis and blow on the wound, and pull it upwards until the head of the penis is inside; then, clean it well of the dirt that has gathered, then tie the wound with a double thread, then tie it under a stitch to another stitch; and hold it with two fingers by the second stitch with the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two stitches, then quickly lift the wound and pull the head of the penis; then let the blood run little by little, for that is the cure; and put powder on it, and over the powder a layer of glue made from a boiled egg, tempered with rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the knives for cleansing is this: the two blades should be sharp and the blade should be as wide as the handle equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the cleansing is when the wound inside is at the incision; then it is necessary that you extend it with your fingernail, before the wound forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it passes three days, and that which is under the penis is swollen, then leave it until the hot abscess is calmed, and gently scrape it; cut it as you can, and be careful of the penis area, it will do no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with the things mentioned in the section on treating wounds, and if the wound is cut beyond measure and it goes upwards, it will not harm; then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Concerning the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Urine retention is caused by blockage by stones, or congealed blood, or pus, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have discussed in the division; and if the urine is not flowing, and you see that the retention is due to a stone lodged in the neck of the bladder, the patient should be bent over their knees, with their feet placed on their back, and the patient's abdomen stretched upwards from the back, and the patient should strain as much as possible.  Then the bladder neck is forced to expel the stone above, so the urine flows out; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient experiences great pain, you should use a surgical instrument called a "syringe" to administer extraction.  Its shape is as follows: it should be made of fine, lightweight silver, like the feather of a bird; and its length should be one and a half palms, and be narrow at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for the release of urine is this: take a double thread, tie a small piece of wool or cotton to one end, and put the threaded end into the syringe; cut off the excess wool, and push it down to the tip of the syringe.  Then lubricate the syringe with oil, butter, and egg white, have the patient sit on a stool, and apply moist olive oil and warm water to the bladder and penis.  Gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root, then pull the penis upwards towards the groin.  Push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and the patient feels it reach the empty space. This is not always done in this order because the passage can be twisted; then pull the thread gently, piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool.  Withdraw the thread, and make the urine flow.  Repeat the process with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Concerning the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or blood appear in the bladder, or putrefaction has gathered, and you wish to apply liquids and remedies, use an instrument called a "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see.  The opening through which the medicine flows should be such that it seals the penis firmly without additional force, so that the moisture can be drawn out and pushed in when needed.  When you wish to inject your medicine into the bladder, place the tip of the instrument into the moisture, and pull the inner part; then draw the moisture to the instrument, and forcefully push the inner part back in; the moisture will enter, and reach the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it; and this is the shape of the slender enema used to treat the bladder: it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or pewter, with the tip higher up; and below it is a single opening, through which the liquid flows.  Then take a sheep's bladder and put the liquid you want to use for the enema into it.  Tie it between the two openings with a strong double thread, and warm that liquid slightly over the fire.  Then insert the tip of the enema into the penis, and press on the bladder with your hand to force all the liquid into it, until the patient feels the liquid reach the bladder. If you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle out of it, and pierce small holes all around it.  Put a strong thread through these holes, stitch the circle together, like a satchel, and put in the oil, liquid, and water you want to use; fasten it into the instrument.  And do as you did with the bladder; press with your hand until the liquid reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone (kidney stone).
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the different types of stones, along with the extraction methods and remedies; and I have described the difference between stones formed in the kidneys and all the symptoms, and what kind of stones require surgical intervention, as well as those in the bladder and urethra; and I will explain it clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones formed in the bladder occur more often in children, and it is a sign that the urine from the bladder resembles water in its subtlety; and sand appears, and the patient rubs their penis, and often bends, and then stiffens; and many of these jumps affect the foundations; and the cure is easier in children up to four years old, and is very difficult in the elderly, and is moderate in those between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the impurities in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift and move them downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes emerges from its upper position; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downward; then search for and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then quickly proceed to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall out by touching completely, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a grown youth; and place it in his fundament, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, pull it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and push it outward to where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to extend his right hand upward to the testicles, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the testicles in the area where the incision will be made; then place the cutting spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between that which is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but along the side of the left groin; and let it be straight over the stone, and your fingers should be near the fundament, and let the cut be wider outward and narrower inward, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure of the fingers at the fundament will cause it to jump out effortlessly; and know that there are stones with angles and edges; these are difficult to remove; and there are some that are round, like a nut, and smooth, from which the removal is easier.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those with angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, you must grasp it with pincers that are like a file at the head, to tighten the stone so that it does not escape; or you place a thin, curved instrument beneath it; and if you cannot remove it thus, enlarge the opening a little, and if the blood flows, stop it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, remove the largest one first to the neck of the bladder, then cut over it, then push it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be chipped, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out repeatedly through the opening because the wound cannot close; however, try to pull or break it with pincers until you remove it in pieces; and when you have finished your work, fill the wound with frankincense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and bandage it tightly, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, over it to soothe the hot swelling; then place the patient on his back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, thoroughly wash the area with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon and basilicon ointments until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot boils occur in the wound, or corrosion or blood clots in the bladder, and urine is retained in such a way that it leaks with the urine, then insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and rot it; then wash the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary, every time you treat him, to tie his legs together and gather the medicines at the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and lodged inside, and the urine cannot come out, treat it as I said before, by cutting it many times, and one is excused from the cutting by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod shaped like this, with three angles forming a single branch.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra below the stone, so that it cannot return into the bladder; then gently insert the rod into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod with your hand, gently against the stone, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; and the urine will immediately flow; then press your hand against the remaining portion of the stone that is inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it is quickly broken and expelled with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this due to any obstacle, tie one thread below the stone and another above, then cut the urethra at the point of the stone between the two threads, then extract it forcefully, and untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone in women.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes stones are found in women, and if this occurs, the cure is difficult, and is prohibited for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman knowledgeable enough to expose her body to examination, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a knowledgeable woman in this art of hands; and the fourth reason is that a woman's stone is deeper than a man's stone, so a deeper incision is needed, and there is significant fear involved. And if necessity demands this, you must take a knowledgeable woman, and she is difficult to find, and if you find no such woman, seek a discreet, chaste woman; and present a wise and experienced woman in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to do what you command her to do in the inquiry about the stone; and carefully consider whether the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should press it against her finger, and instruct her to place her finger in the opening of the afflicted woman, and search for it and press her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the opening of the bladder down, until she reaches the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh, in the middle of the opening where the stone is located, and feel the stone in that area; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and the incision should initially be small; then insert a tool into the incision, if you feel the stone, widen the wound until the stone can be extracted forcefully, and know that many types of stones exist: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	So you will know the signs to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood overwhelms you, apply crushed vitriol to the area, and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work, until the stone is forcibly removed, and have the instruments I mentioned for the extraction of stones in men to aid you in your work; and if the blood overwhelms you, and it is from a cut artery, apply the powder to the area, and bind it with bandages, and do not begin again, and leave the stone and do not remove it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the area is healed, return to your work until the stone is forcibly removed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery hernia is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white substance, beneath the skin of the testicles, containing the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly within the shell of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and that matter spreads.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: sometimes it is a color leaning towards jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often; and these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it is in the white syfac that we mentioned, the abscess is round, a little long like the shape of an egg, and the testicles are not apparent, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper shell, the abscess is round with a part of the egg, and for this one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white syfac, one feels it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, test throughout the entire, narrow space, whose shape is previously described.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, that comes after the probing, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be bled according to their ability and the fullness of their body; then lay them on their back, on something a little high, and put many cloths underneath; then sit on their left side, and tell the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the testicles' core; then take the lancet, and cut the skin of the testicles along its length up to the edge of the blade, and let your incision be straight in dividing the skin of the testicles down to the white syfac, and scrape it subtly according to your ability; then pierce the white syfac full of water with one wide opening, and drain all the water, and then put your forceps, and extend the syfac upward; and do not touch the core of the testicles, but only the syfac; cut all or by pieces, even the side of it subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return; and if the egg is forced out by your work, put it back in place when you have completed the work on the syfac; then bring the two edges of the testicles' core together with a stitch, then treat it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another ailment, you must tie the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the outflow of blood; then cut the testicle at the entire suspensory, and remove the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if water has gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches; cut the other part just as you did the first, likewise, then wipe the blood, and put moistened wool in rose oil in the wound; and put more wool soaked in wine and oil over the two testicles, and place doubled cloths over that, and tie it tightly at the entire band that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with shredded wool according to this appearance, and have them joined by stitching at the waistband of the breeches, and one of the ends should rest over the buttocks down to the back, and the other to the part of the blade; and the other two ends over the two hips, and let the entire constriction be gathered in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this branch is treated with cautery in place of an iron cut, and you should take a small, knife-like cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we have said, so that the white syfac that contains the water is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac with the forceps, and scrape it with this sharp heated cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut it in every way you can, until you drain everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and be wary of blood leakage, and more wary than the work of cutting; and if anything makes you wary, or an abscess, or blood leakage, or anything else, treat what makes you wary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is afraid and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, administer a puncture, as I tell you, and this is that when you are certain, through the signs we have mentioned, that the watery branch is present, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part, right over the entire wide spatumile, and make the puncture at the length of the body; and let the opening be wide, so that all the water runs out; then place cotton over the area and tie it, and leave it to drain the remaining water, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the linen bandage does not allow the water to leave through the opening of the wound, then you must insert a quill or the instrument used to draw water from hydropetic patients, of which the form is shown before; and widen the wound a little, and know that the water will return and gather after six months or in that time, and when it gathers as before, and so the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the treatment of this branch there is fear in many situations, so I think it is better to leave it; and I will tell you the treatment and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and especially to the testicles; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say, by an excess of acrid and sharp humour, which spreads to the testicles, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and does not show any pain, and is a serious abscess; and perhaps some abscesses are frightening and painful, and of a fixed color, and sometimes come from a rupture of an artery, or from swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a rupture of an artery, it is recognized by the hot nature of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	The one made from swelling of the vein is recognized by its nature when pressed by the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the incision on this appearance, and on other flesh; and you should cut the root of the testicles, then lift the testicle upwards, and cut the white covering around it, and free the suspensory ligament from all sides of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the testicle is already fused with the surrounding tissues, then you must pull the testicle and cut it; and if there is air on the surface, or within the vessels, you must free all that membrane and cut it cleanly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the base of the flesh is in the rear, you must cut it completely and remove the testicle, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess, surrounded by a swelling similar to a boil, with softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when he moves; and the treatment for this illness is just as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and nonetheless, we will tell you the method, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must have the patient sit on a raised seat, then have him place the suspensory for the testicles down towards his fingers, encompassing all vessels near the penis, and the master should hold them firmly; then cut with a sharp, wide scalpel through the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then cauterize from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries found in the temples; then insert a needle with a double thread, tying it to the first point where the pus has appeared, and tie it again to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and drain the corrupt fluids; then treat the wound as with other suppurating wounds, so that no vessels are severed supplying either testicle; for this will not cause any harm. If pus is present in all the vessels, then the testicles must be removed from all vessels, so that the testes do not lose their nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the symphysis.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	This affliction arises from the separation at the symphysis pubis, or from stretching in the abdominal region near the groin, causing the intestines to descend from the rupture toward one of the testicles.  This rupture is either of the symphysis itself, or of its stretching, and these two conditions result from many causes: impact, jumping, straining, lifting heavy objects, and similar things.  The signs when it's due to stretching of the symphysis are that it happens gradually over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are uniform, even towards the deeper portions, because the symphysis compresses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it's due to the separation of the symphysis are that it causes sudden pain at the onset, and the abscesses appear differently, under the skin close to the surface, due to the escape of the intestines and the body's pushing away from the symphysis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the hernia, and are retained within, causing the patient great suffering, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is cause for fear, so one should avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of treatment is that you instruct the patient to push the intestines back into the wound with your hand if possible; then the patient should lie on their back, with their thighs raised; then extend the scrotum upwards, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise; then insert forceps as needed to open the wound, so that the testicles may exit; then scrape the symphysis which is under the skin of the testicles until the hard white symphysis is exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger into what is under the testicle, between the white hard symphysis and the underlying second symphysis, and separate what is behind the testicle and the second symphysis; then use your right hand to push inside the scrotum, and extend the white hard symphysis upwards with your left hand, and lift the testicle with the entire symphysis towards the groin; and instruct the assistant to extend the testicle upwards, and loosen what is behind the ligament; and with your fingers, see if any intestines are wrapped around the white hard symphysis, and if you find any, push it back into the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the back part of the symphysis, which is behind the skin of the testicles; after the groin, then cut the ends of the threads until there are four threads; then join them together in the form of a cross, and tie the symphysis, which we mentioned, under the skin of the testicles, with a strong knot on both sides; then wrap the ends of the threads and tie them tightly on both sides so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter, preventing a painful abscess; and place the bandage again, according to the first bandage, extending two fingers beyond; and after these two bandages, leave a space of one finger of symphysis under the scrotum; and after all the rest, according to the roundness of the testicle; then cut into the area below the skin of the testicles until the blood flows and the swelling subsides, as we said before; then apply oiled wool to the wounds and apply the bandage we have described.
