Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white symphysis we mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of excessive bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leaves the bandage until it falls off by itself; and if it takes too long to fall off, it should be soaked in warm water, and apply what we have said, until it falls off; then treat the wound with another treatment until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this instance, I never saw anyone dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done as if the hernias that are interconnected, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision above or slightly below; then cut it in half, and treat the abscess with what you have opened, until the vessels fall out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the area opens; and none of the intestines descend into the scrotum, and if any do, it is little, and it repairs itself every hour; however, if it stays too long in this condition, the wound or the sac grows, until the intestine descends; and this happens due to the extension of the sac that is in the groin, as we have said, for it is stretched, then softened and swollen the area and it opens; and the treatment is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way: and it is that the patient lies often on their back between your hands, then cut the area of the ruptured swollen area of the width of three fingers; and then remove the sac underneath the skin that surrounds it, then take the rait (a tool) and put it over the visible area of the sac; and press it into the deep part of the abdomen, then sew the two visible areas of the sac over the head of the rait, and stitch one and the other; then remove the head of the rait, and do not cut the sac or stretch the egg or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines; then treat it with the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sac is constricted, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is milder in this area, and closer to a cure.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum is softened in some men, because the tissues within are softened, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on their back, and cuts the softened skin over the natural skin; then joins the two edges with stitches, and if you wish, stitch first the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and the thread falls out.
dou chastrement	of the chastening
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that chastening is forbidden in our law, and for that reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary except for two reasons: one is that the wise man should know how to answer when asked, and should know the cure; and the other is that we often need to chasten certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that chastening is done in two ways: either by pulling or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by pulling, we make the beast sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and hanging; then we take them in your hand, until they are reset and you feel no more pain.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastening of the testicles: you must restrain the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each testicle in one cut, when you have well scored them; and leave a little bit of the surface and the subtle surface that is over the vessels; and this manner of chastening is milder than that which is done by pulling, because with the pulling, perhaps some of the testicles remain, by which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways in men: one is that between the two testicles there appears also the shape of a woman's nature, or there are hairs, and sometimes urine flows from it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and have a penis like a rod and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure for both man and woman is to cut all the attached flesh and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tensigene
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is an attached flesh on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must remove the excess tentigene with your hand or forceps, and cut it slightly; and do not go too deep, lest blood flow, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and there is another flesh that grows at the mouth of the womb, and fills it, and possibly leaks, and resembles a pouch, and for this reason the ancients called it "pouch disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If necessary, you must cut it, as we said of the tentigene, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of the erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the woman's nature is not pierced, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident from a disease that has arrived; or it is by attached flesh, or a subtle or thick cyst, and is formed deep within the womb, or on the sides, or below, or wherever; and it hinders conception, and childbirth, and possibly the ability to bear flowers; and the knowledge of this is through observation of the discharge.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is readily apparent, then apply your fingers or a tool.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle cyst, and it is close to the two lips, then hurry, and do this: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, her legs spread; then gently stretch the two lips, until the subtle cyst is rounded, and the swelling is open; then take wool, and soak it in oil, and place it over the area, and let the woman lie on her side each day, so that it cannot close up.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the cyst is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula, resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of newly grown flesh, then suspend it with a forceps and cut it; and have blood-stopping medicines, such as dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white; then apply a wide lead strip, so that the wound cannot close; and let it remain for a long time, and apply a dry linen tent; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when new flesh grows in the sore, it must be cut according to this method, if it is not an infected abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an infected abscess in the sore, one should not apply fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood flows habitually, and when the hemorrhoids are old, they become painful; and we have already discussed their similarities, signs, and I will now describe those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and pain, when they are deep within the sore and do not appear on the surface, are not to be treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the sore, which can be felt, are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must put the woman in a cold room, then grasp the painful area with tongs and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle over it medicines that constrict blood, such as oak galls, dragon's blood, and frankincense, and similar things; then put her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if a discharge of blood comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, gallnuts, and similar things, and then take barley flour and mix it with honey and egg white, and make a poultice for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts, without inflicting injury; then take wool and soak it in plantain juice or agrimony juice mixed with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so it must be cut, as I said of the painful swelling; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the breast.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the breast, such as sores, stony abscesses, herpes, boil-like sores, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and several other illnesses which I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to describe in this treatise the hot abscess which occurs in the breast, which is not among those abscesses that collect pus; and if you wish to know the treatment, observe if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red, you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and let them have two small seats where they lean, and rest on their back and bring their feet to the outer parts of the leg; and let their thighs be spread out, and place their arms under their knees, and bind them well with a good bandage; then support them towards the right side, and administer the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the breast, of which the shape comes later; and it is necessary that when you wish to administer this instrument, you first insert the rod to know the depth of the breast, so that what enters the instrument does not go deeper than it should and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the breast with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt them; and it is necessary for them to place the horn of the instrument above, and for them to hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one cuts it with a soft hand, one must cut it at the head, at the level of the skin; and when the pus is emptied, it is necessary to place in the wound softened cloths in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and place the cloth deep in the wound, in the hollow of the breast, and place over the breast and the incision clean wool soaked in water or cooked mallows; then treat it after two days of suitable ointment, until it is healed; and sometimes the breast and wound are cleaned with an enema of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and long aristolochia, which have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is reopened in the breast, it is necessary to avoid using iron, but treat it as we have described in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the natural form of childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing downwards and wanting to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural form, and the child comes out under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her abdomen so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends under its head, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the breast is cleared of its superfluities by good cleansing; and that which comes out otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes out on its feet, and the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes out on its stomach, or backwards, and is turned perhaps on its neck, and by other bad forms; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and to avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the forms of how to help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by a natural birth, and the woman is giving birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, have her sit on a stool, or let women hold her; and arouse her nature with oil or boiled fenugreek, and then let the midwife place the small spatula, of which the shape is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the afterbirth, and cut with her fingernail until the moisture that is within comes out; and grasp the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to administer an enema to the woman of fenugreek gruel with sesame oil; then have her drink and sneeze with ginger, and keep her mouth and nostrils closed for an hour: the child will now come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, it is necessary that you gently bring them back piece by piece; and if they cannot go in, put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up; then lower the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when it is lowered; and if the hands cannot go in, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is mentioned before, and pull out the child, and put it back in place as well.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's birth on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, it must be pushed upward; and then it is turned little by little until it is straight; then take one of the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps down to the thighs, instruct her to grasp it, and make her sneeze with ginger; if it jumps out, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come out as we have said, turn it slowly, until it is according to its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take a mixture of aloe, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all together in a mortar; and put on the woman's body and to drive out this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is softened underneath, make her a compress of myrrh and put it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and pinch her mouth and nose, and gently press her stomach, for the child will now jump out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's issue upon her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, the midwife should place her hands gently; then be held on her lap, and the child's feet hanging down, and lying on a bed; and gently fold her hands, and then grasp the hands on her stomach, and remove the cushions underneath, until she is prepared for delivery; and if the child does not jump out, take its feet and move them forcefully, then move the stomach upwards, then push with your hands; and gently pull the child out; and instruct the woman to strain until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out from the large, one hand hanging down.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to devise a way to bring the hand back; if it cannot be brought back, make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her on a bed and forcefully straighten her legs; then administer the mixture I have described; and if she does not deliver, make her sit on a seat, then attempt to bring the hand back; and extract the child according to its natural position, make her sneeze, and instruct her to strain until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's issue on its mother's lap, with its arms outstretched, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	The midwife should hold the child's hand, then gently turn it, and gently pull it out; and when it is equal, place the specified mixture of herbs and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move slightly; and when this is done, make her sit on a seat and instruct her to strain; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner for the entire afterbirth.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way, for the entire afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your fingernail, until the moisture is emptied; and if the child hangs by its face and neck, cut it from the bottom, so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then place the child inside, until you have positioned it correctly, and instruct the woman to strain several times; then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, unless few; I know that they are multiple, and are separated by a membrane that divides them, which is attached to the bottom; and sometimes they issue as naturally as a single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue with difficulty, treat them as we have said, and let the midwife be skillful, and do quickly and easily what she must do; and do so as it befits their health.
de plusors enfans	Of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or many as many as fifteen, and they are all formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the wise, glorious one, and it is necessary for the midwife to know all of this, for perhaps similar things happen to her; so do as it is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman with a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to manual work; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; then it is necessary that the woman be supported on her back, and her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister should hold her from two sides, or she should be bound to the bed so that she is not pulled during the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with the mucilage of elder and fenugreek and linseed, then let the midwife anoint her hands with these oils and mucilages; then gently place them in the womb, then find a place where she inserts the hooks that are suitable for this, and watch if the child is prepared to descend from its head; then insert the hooks into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the groin or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, then insert it in the groin and in the middle ribs; and it is necessary that she hold the hook in her right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of her left hand, and gently place her whole hand on it, and insert the hook in any of these places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty place; and this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert another hook, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch it equally by moving from one side to the other, to make it come out, and let the hooks be toothed to hold it, as here is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, then let the midwife anoint some of her fingers with oil, and place them on that part, and pull the other part; and if any remains, then place this hook in a higher place, and do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be drawn back due to constriction, then it is necessary that you wrap it in a cloth, until it all comes out; then cut it at the joint of the sole or with a knife, and likewise you must do with the other hand, and with the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and the passage is narrow, or it has a sharp point, then you must place the pointed spatula between your fingers, and split the head and remove the point; or you may round it with the instrument called "almidach," whose form comes with the instruments in the chapter following this; and likewise do the same if the child has a large natural head; and then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the head is stuck and constricted in the groin, then it should be split, so that the moisture that is in it comes out; and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the extraction is light, and the correction to the mother's mouth is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tight in the belly or the breast, you must extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and split the belly or breast, until the moisture within flows out; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, the midwife should place her hand deep inside the mother's body and pull it toward the mother's mouth; then insert a hook or two, and pull it out; and if the mother's mouth is constricted by a hot abscess that has formed there, then no effort should be made, but rather moist and greasy things should be administered; and apply poultices, and soak in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, administer what we have said about a living child; and if one does not have the power, pull it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, administer what we have said about hot abscesses that come in the mother; and if bleeding occurs, put it in constricting water, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a child had died, then another was conceived on top of that one, and the other died as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess appeared in the jaw, and swelled until it opened, and began to fester greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and pondered it for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong-drawing plaster, and one bone came out, and after a few days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly surprised, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was bones from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound, and extracted many bones, until the woman was in a better condition; and the woman lived for a long time like that, and a little pus would often come from the place; and I have recounted this chapter only because, when masters encounter something strange, they should know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the marrow back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here after comes the shape of the press, with which one squeezes the books; and with two turns at the two heads of the two ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be one finger wide, and the margin of the wood one finger, and a palm and a half long; and between the two ligaments should be two joints of this same wood, which should be fastened to one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two joints are put into the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pincers; and have at its two heads two joints, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the marrow with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, feet dangling and legs open, then place the two joined joints into the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then operate your hand with the entire instrument, as you did with the pincers likewise, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the marrow, so that the marrow does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all surmounted, and their appearances are multiplied; and when the master has them prepared, the work is all the more rapid, and higher in regard to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not neglect the instrument until you have prepared it, for their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with a strong stimulus, and hold her hands over her mouth and nose; and if she expels it by this, so much the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, she takes a pot and makes a hole in its lid, and places herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are boiled in water over the fire; then she places one end of a reed into the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marrow, and holds it until the vapors reach the marrow; then she makes her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The afterbirth will expel quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if, after this treatment, it remains and is not expelled, instruct the woman to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in the juice of mallow, and then apply it to the area, and search for the afterbirth; and when she has found it, she should gently and slowly pull it outward, so that the marrow does not break during the extraction; but it must be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pulled; it will come out and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marrow is still constricted, we have described the treatment of sneezing and the fumigation of herbs; and if none of this works, be careful not to force the extraction; but you should bind that which is at the mouth of the marrow to the woman's thigh, and then administer a clyster of tetrafarmacon ointment; this will soften it and put it back in place, and it will be expelled; however, if it softens, a foul odor will arise in the stomach and head, and harm the woman.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations are necessary for this: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of the flowers and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles a chain, and one places the thin end in the area, and the wide ends over the fire; and let the fumigation be over the embers, and continue until it is exhausted, and then begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their fundament pierced, but it is blocked by a thin membrane: then it is necessary for the nurse to pierce that membrane with her finger, and not to pierce it with a sharp instrument, and to avoid touching the surrounding area. Then put soaked wool in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear it will close again, place a lead chain in the opening, and leave it in place for some days, and remove it when the child wants to go to the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these blockages come from the closing of a wound or abscess; therefore, that closing must be cut: it should be treated as we have described with the lead chain.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from beneath the fundament are swellings, and those that come from beside the fundament, or in the space between the two parts, have one or more fistulas; and when that swelling is old, it opens, and there is either white or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are open; and they are known by the fact that there is discharge or flatulence when the patient has a bowel movement, and sometimes a worm escapes.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce down to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they extend to the hip joint, and to the base of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows a penetrating fistula from the fundament, and one that is not penetrating: and that is if you insert your index finger into the fundament, and put a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, you put a thin lead tent or a horsehair into it until you feel the tent or hair against your finger; and if you don't feel it, and there is no discharge, flatulence, or worm from the opening, as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates to the bladder or to the urinary tract, urine leaks from it, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces to the hip joint, the tent reaches the place; if there is no tortuosity and the pain is localized around it, it is often that a boil arises, and no medicine or ointment will mend it.  In these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure but labor, and the vanity of foolish charlatans who meddle in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not penetrating and not old, there is hope for health through iron, as I have experienced.  The patient lies on their back, with legs raised to the hips, and hips tilted towards the stomach. Then insert a bronze or lead tent, if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent reaches.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it near the foundation, you should insert your index finger.  If you then feel the tent has pierced it, and a surface or flesh is uncovered between your finger, know then that it is penetrating; then do not attempt treatment for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says however that some can be healed, but this is rare.  The help given involves heating the thin cautery according to the width of the fistula, as previously stated; and place it hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the foundation.  Repeat this two or three times, until you know that the decayed flesh, resembling a bird's feather, has been burned.  Then treat with moistened tents in butter until the flesh comes off, and then treat with ointment to generate new flesh and close the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters, but does not pierce the finger on the foundation, and there is a thick layer of flesh or surface between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula where the covering is on the core; then cut it from the beginning of the fistula, and advance the tent, and then follow with the cautery, until it reaches the end of the tent.  And the tent will be delivered and fall out; then clean the decayed flesh, resembling a bird's feather, and leave nothing of it.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood flows between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cauterization by fire brings together two good things: namely, the burning of the stuck flesh, and the stopping of blood and drying of the moisture.  Then treat with tents moistened in butter or crushed herbs, until the area gives off pus, and the burned flesh comes out in the pus; then treat the wound with ointments that heal and generate strong flesh, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and will not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula goes down to the base and is far from the body, put your finger on the base and explore it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between it and the cloth or surface or flesh, where it is close to piercing, there is no other way but hope and expectation, through the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the bottom, or if you can, put tents in and treat it as before; and do not go too deep, lest you sever the tendon that holds the base, and the pus comes out without your intent. Then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse it since it is cut away from the base, either with a tent or another suitable instrument; then cleanse the wounded flesh in the wound as much as you can; then try to restore the wound and keep the fistula outside the base: this will be an easier thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are like this: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the base next to the skin above, take a tent pierced at the head according to this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put one thread twisted into two, and put the tent through all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing into the margin of the base inside, then pull the thread from that hole, as you put your finger on the base; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and tighten one to the other, and leave it for one or two days; and tighten it sometimes, until the thread cuts the flesh that is between the two, and they fall out; then treat the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make it cut so deep by the lacing, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatumile spine, with which one pierces the fistula, is very sharp on one side and sharp, and not on the other, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two types: either they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and often bleed, and there are one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and they often drip or a little bit of yellow liquid or a little blood, and they have the color of the body; and the treatment of those who have them inside the fundament is that you tell the patient to strain himself to go to the chamber pot, until the fundament lets them out, and the thread appears; hurry, and pinch them with the tongs, or hold them with your nail, then cut them at their roots; and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamelot; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle some warm powders on them that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the cautery chapter, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, then give the patient a mordant and harsh clyster to wash what is in the fundament, so that it can come out clearly; when the patient strains, and the threads are outside the fundament, the treatment is easy; and that you take them with your nail or tongs, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and that they fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must administer the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread above and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one to drain the excess blood; then put a damp cloth on the fundament in rose oil or in ointment, and put it on the fundament, and tell the patient to rest; and then leave it until they fall, and when they have fallen, treat them with ointment and other remedies, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the filth in the fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying of filth in the intestine, and through constriction of nature, and when the patient is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should scrape the scab off with a spatula or your fingernail, so that it doesn't get moist; then treat it until it is healed properly; and if it cannot heal, then repeat the scraping more forcefully than before, until it bleeds a lot and is raw; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the shivering
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small, deceptive appearance around the body, and goes deep within; and sometimes one finds cold, and feels it like a deathly shivering, which spreads through the whole body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is to take a stick of goose feather, or a strong eagle's feather, and place that stick over the shivering, so that the circle of the feather encompasses the shivering entirely; then rotate your hand around the stick, until you cut all around the shivering, and drive it deep, and remove the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one of copper or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin underneath and pointed on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not piercing, in order to hold and press it on the finger.  And if you wish, cauterize the shivering, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or gold, or of molten or hammered copper; and sometimes these instruments are made small or large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those, then, that are administered in the treatment of children and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is thus wide at the top, where the belly is wrapped in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a separation where the belly is wrapped, as you see, and the bottom is pierced; and there are two holes on one side, and one on the other; and the belly, where the medicines are put, should be of an animal's bladder or parchment, and be pierced all around with small holes, and have a space of one inch between each hole; then, put a strong thread into each hole, knotted around in an X or similar figure, and assemble the belly as if it were a sheep's; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the clyster; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And the medicine should neither be too hot nor too cold, and grease the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or something similar, then gently insert it; then the minister squeezes it together with both hands until it is completely empty, then remove the clyster, and the patient raise their legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, he should hold it as long as he can; and if he sleeps a full night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer the clyster in a disease of stomach discharge, and the medicine is quick to come out, then repeat it until the patient is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or abscess, then the clyster should be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin is tightened:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds; now we shall tell you the treatments for hands and medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of stones, and cuts from swords and knives, or from lances or wood or arrows, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as wounds that fall on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and will begin with simple head wounds, for the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if it is from the throwing of stones or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless broken and the wound is large, and you fear a hot abscess: you should immediately make it bleed from the cephalic vein, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side of the injured area; and keep the patient from overeating wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to bleed, let his diet be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and place on the wound, if a hot abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not discolored by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if the burn has discolored it, place some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut and similar things, and the edges cannot be brought together by tents, bring them together by stitching, as I will explain for wounds of the belly, of the chest.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a little, cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore strong flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as hard-boiled eggs and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rot in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, cut all the rot out, and cauterize it, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, seek out the artery, and if you find it dislodged, tie it off with a thread; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: and it is that you put this powder in, which welds before the burn has discolored it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; living coals three parts, and powder it finely, and fill the wound with it, and bind it tightly until it heals well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with coals alone, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the burn has not discolored the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has discolored the wound, especially in its state, one does not put this powder on it; but puts on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it becomes sticky; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
