Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, bind it with fine pincers; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy than to let it heal, and put nothing constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is also with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be soft, like warm washes in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and cupped washes also in soft water, and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, stitch it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is festering and full of pus, pierce it in a lower place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes from it, cauterize it and bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the channels are kept through which the food passes, stitch the heart to the lining of the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it to its natural shape; and then restrict the flow, and leave it for several days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all the ones that you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave until the wound rots, and the exit is loosened and straightened; and if the wound is fresh, dust it with the powder that I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, observe if gas escapes from the wound when the patient breathes; then know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it, because the blood may not drain deep, return to the heart and kill the patient; but apply an attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three, or four, or more days; thus there will be no spasms, nor tremors or tightening of the breath; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then treat it with poultices and other remedies until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and opens again, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or in the chest or back, treat it as was described previously; if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is embedded in the bone, and has broken pieces, cleanse the wound, and remove them if they are detached; and if they are not detached, let the wound fester, as this will ease the removal; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large, medium, and small; in the large wound, sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, causing their involvement; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because one puts the intestines back more painfully if they are not returned quickly; for the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, making it more difficult to return them to their place, and thus the medium wound is more troublesome, because one must return the intestines to their place than in other cases.  And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four types: two common sutures occur in the suturing of the belly, and the suturing of other wounds of the body, and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds; and yet they are more appropriate with the suturing of the belly, and I will explain each and clarify them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, and it is difficult to put it back, it is for one of these two reasons: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: soak a sponge or a linen cloth in lukewarm water, or cook in water with squill, cypress, and spikenard, and rinse the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes use wine that tightens and is better than water alone to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or cooked mallows and elderberries, for this makes entry easier with little effort; and if it cannot enter, then slit the wound a little with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than the incision, for no one should make an incision without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting it: cut inwards along the curve and not outwards, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes, return it back according to its natural form to its proper place, if you are able, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, focus on making the wounded part higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to administer what I say for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply what is appropriate, then take a gentle hand that holds the entire rupture, and brings the edges together; and this is the common method of stitching, and is that you take a needle or several, according to the size of the wound, then leave an inch of space from the beginning of the wound, and put a needle or good strong thread in it; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the flesh underneath, as far as you make it penetrate, and bring together the two edges of the flesh and the four together; then wrap a double thread around the needle from both sides, then bring the two edges of the wound together, and then leave an inch of space, and put in another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this, according to your need for needles, until the entire wound is tightened; and the needles should be medium-sized, between fine and thick, for fine needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they must be medium-sized; and it is not appropriate to push the needles too far outside the flesh and skin, so that they cut and reopen the wound before it is stitched; and then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient while they sleep, and place swabs or cloths on the ends of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for one or two needles will suffice.  The second method of stitching is common, and is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the flesh with a needle that has a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced all four edges together, pull the needle back to the part where you began, in the manner in which clothes are sewn; and put a distance of the width of a little finger between each stitch; this stitch is known by men, and I stitched a wound that a man had in his stomach, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in size, and the intestines were protruding by over two palms in size, and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was stitched up until 15 days later, and I treated it, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat it with ointment, because I was in a place where none was found, nor any medicine; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you two proper methods of stitching: take the needle, and push it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the flesh straight through, then leave the edge of the flesh where you put the needle, and make it pierce from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch just as the skinners do leather, and that you leave the flesh on one side, and take it again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is as some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and place one edge of the flesh against the other, in this way: put a needle into the edge of the wound near the edge, and pierce only that place, and leave the two edges of the flesh; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside to the inside, through the two edges of the flesh; then pierce each from the outside to the inside, in two other edges of the wound that are on the other side; and this is the most subtle method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this, and some testify, that one should stitch the belly with two needles, or with a thread on each; and one should put one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who stitch straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the wound is like the treatment of other wounds: and when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, before the ulcer has changed it, put the intestine back in place and stitch it; then apply a powder that stops the bleeding, and if the ulcer has changed it, apply any available ointment until the wound suppurates; and when the thread comes out, and the flesh and the wound are closed, then treat the wound as the others until it is healed; and if you don't have medicine, put on old cotton as soon as it begins to suppurate, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound might spread to the main limbs, you should moisten light wool in tempered oil, or in rose oil, and put it around the joints and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or rot in the boils, which often happens, give enemas of warmed black wine, especially if the rot reaches the intestine; and pierce it internally, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the abundance of veins in it, and due to the delicacy of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the nerve jumps out of the wound, put it back in place like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and become dark or black, you must tie the black area so that blood does not flow, because there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the tie, and hang the two ends from the part below the wound, outwards to facilitate extraction when the nerve falls out, and the wound suppurates.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the boil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, for I saw that a man was wounded in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became festered and turned into a fistula, and there were emissions of waste and gas; I applied treatment according to what I could, and I did not cease to treat until it was healed and the area was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it close, I feared the patient might have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take a strong thread with large ends, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the thread has opened its mouth, place it over the two edges so that it tightens its mouth over them; and then cut off the end, and this will stay so that it cannot detach, then put another thread in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and then stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This intestine can be healed without harm to the patient, and the intestine can be tied with a thin thread taken from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this thread of intestine that is very lean, and then tie to this end a thin twisted linen thread, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it together into the rupture; and this method of stitching with threads is only as good as the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the large intestines, there is no skill or remedy but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is universally called a "fistula," especially when it is festered and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula, in truth, is a hard, white, festering sore where there is no pain, and is as festered as a bird's feather; and sometimes it discharges clear pus, and sometimes thick; sometimes little, and sometimes quite a bit; and I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound which does not heal, and where there is no flesh, is only due to one of these eight causes: namely, by the weakness of the blood or body; or by its bad quality; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, that does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good for the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because the digestion is slow in the region, and healing is delayed, and it swells by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to show you the treatment of a fistula that is done by manual labor.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the surface, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and some come from the nature of the main limb and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is a fistula that does not come to the place I have mentioned, and you are confident in the cure, and you wish to know it, take a tin or iron probe; if the fistula is straight, seek it out; and if the fistula is crooked, search it with a thin lead probe, because lead bends easily around the curve; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot find it well with probes, irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture flows from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then search it carefully as much as possible, to find out if there is bone or nerve, and is festered deeply; and ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press your hand on them, and the place where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, cut it according to what I have told you, and remove the festering and the corrupt flesh that is inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep and straight, you must cut deeply as much as you can, then place moistened probes with sharp medicine and insert them to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments to promote healthy flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not bother the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, cleanse it until all corruption is removed, then treat it with things that promote flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and pus returns as before, know that you have not reached the bottom: uncover and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with pliers, pull it out with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, and leave none; and if the moisture causes you trouble, and there is no mistake or fear, cut through the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, put something on the wound to promote decay, and leave it until the area around the bones is rotten, and then the bones will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, remove only the corruption until all blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if a large portion of the corrupt material reaches the bone marrow, it must be cleaned and cut all the way to the corruption, and then treated until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of around 30 years, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that arose inside the body, until the matter reached the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to delay opening it; but the doctors, in their folly, worked so much on it that the abscess opened, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared that all discharged pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors applied treatment for two years, and there was no wise person in the art who could help, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed through the openings in large quantities; and the young man's body turned red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one connected to another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened, then, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached the bone within; I cleaned the part of the corrupted bone that appeared to me, and thought there was no other corruption, except what I removed; and began to restore the wound with healing medicines for a long time, and it could not heal; and then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and cleaned and removed it, and tried to mend the place; but I could not, until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and extracted it completely, along with all its marrow, then I restored it with medicines; and he was healed and mended quickly, and no further work was required, except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and because of the fear of death I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the blood evacuation, he often gasped, but he was completely healed, and hard flesh grew in place of the bone, and he was in good condition and had no harm or difficulty at all, neither in movement nor in any other way.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this way: take a bandage, and tie it to the end of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to stretch it upwards; and place another bandage of wool, thicker than the first, and bind it over the flesh that is on top of the bone, stretching the end so that you pull the corrupted flesh away, and expose the flesh over the place where you wish to treat, so that the treatment does not injure the flesh; and place a hot ember or a wooden board under the bone to help cut away the corrupted flesh; and continue cleaning as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and clean again later.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not show, and the corruption is inside or in a part, expose all the flesh; then place a hot ember underneath, and then clean the corruption from one side to the other, and let the cleaning be the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut away the corrupted joint, and clean the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut; and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand, or the finger of the foot, that is a very serious matter, but nevertheless you must examine that corruption, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but so that the veins or nerves do not hinder you; and know that the instruments for cutting and cleaning these bones are various, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore you must prepare a tool for each kind of work; and know that the work itself will show you the tool you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the evidence of the types of illnesses; so consider which tool you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder might rot either from internal causes or from external fire; and when you have treated this corruption with medicinal cures, and they do not work, you must cut that limb down to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, the loss of the limb; and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as though it were burned by fire, and will rot after the blackness; then this corruption spreads from limb to limb, and takes hold of the whole body; so hurry to cut, and if it is from the sting of some venomous creatures, like sea scorpions, vipers, and similar ones, if the corruption is in the tip of the finger, cut it off, and do not allow it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no remedies are of any use except according to the amount of their virtue; and do the same when the corruption reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut below the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut off the entire foot; and if it goes up the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it goes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or cleaning the limb is that you bind it above and below, and have some assistants pull one bandage down, and others pull the other bandage up, and separate the flesh between the two bandages with a wide spatula, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or clean, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the cleaning does not touch the healthy part, and cause further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some astringent powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man on his foot: he had a blackness that appeared to be a burning by fire, and that corruption first reached his toe on the foot, until it affected the whole foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he quickly cut off his foot, and was healed; and a long time afterward, the corruption returned to the finger of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied things that cause a rebound after cleansing the body, and the corruption could not stop; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he might die, for the man's strength was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I have recounted this only so that one might do likewise, if there is need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess appears in a fleshy area, and it remains so long that it gathers a large amount of pus; and then it bursts and the pus escapes, and the area remains empty, like a vessel; and the skin above it is as thin as a delicate cloth, and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sinus," and not "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, it is called "fistula"; and the treatment is that you cut the skin all around it, especially when it is thin, like a cloth; and it will not heal through its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you suspect that the skin will heal, that the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it with a clyster like this:  Observe if the sinus is large and the pus that comes out has a foul odor, then clyster it with Egyptian medicine, made thus: Take ash, oil, and litharge, all in equal amounts, and place the ingredients in a vessel over heat until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take some of this as needed, and mix it in water or honey, and clyster the sinus, and constrict the opening; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this repeatedly until the sinus is cleansed and the foul odor removed; and sometimes it is clysted with ash water, when this medicine isn't available, and this is made by taking vine wood ash, pouring water over it, and letting it settle, and then clystering it until you know that the sinus is thoroughly cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate Egyptian medicine or ash water, clyster with water and honey, or a little crushed litharge; or you can clyster with honey and mixed wine, where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine causes the sinus to heal; and when you have done this and are confident that the sinus is clean, clyster it with something that promotes flesh growth. This is done with a diaphanitic plaster mixed with rose oil and wine; or you can clyster with certain medicines and ointments, whose properties I have discussed in the treatment of ointments; and if the opening of the sinus is small, and the clyster tube cannot enter, widen it slightly with an iron tool, and place a piece of Egyptian or basilicon ointment inside the sinus to enlarge it; and if the wound is too wide, close it, leaving just enough space for the clyster to enter, and if the opening that discharges pus is on top, cut or make the opening lower than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the pus is deep, it does not allow the flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the sinus from below as desired, prepare it in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest point, because when the pus is deep, it does not allow the flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the sinus from below as desired, prepare it in such a way that the pus flows easily downwards, and do not leave any pus behind; and take consolidating medicines to put over the sinus, and place a linen cloth over the entire sinus; then cut the wound slightly wider than the opening of the sinus, then spread a soft ointment over another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the opening of the sinus to ease the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except once after several days; and the one that is over the opening of the sinus, remove frequently to remove the pus, and know if the pus that comes out is venom or a little or enough, digested or indigested; and observe if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your treatment has progressed in this manner, and you see the nature that comes out of the opening of the sinus, you will know that the sinus is healing and approaching health; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, replace the cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the sinus discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the sinus will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom flows out after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose wounds are slow to grow flesh, and others who experience the opposite; and if undigested pus comes out of the sinus after many days, know that the sinus will not heal; and if the sinus is slow to heal and is prolonged, add drying medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphanitic ointment, for it contains a significant amount of vitriol, and it is the last resort; take diaphanitic ointment, mix it with rose oil and diluted with equal amounts of old wine; then refine it and use it; and the same thing is better when cooked with honey, if diaphanitic ointment is unavailable, or you take myrrh, aloe, and frankincense, grind them and powder them over the honey while it is over heat; and then glue it to a cloth, and spread it over the sinus, and sometimes an experienced physician will apply long herbs, and roots of the lily of the valley, which is like the flour of vetches and centaury; and use these herbs or mixtures: grind them and make powder, and place it on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it; and if the treatment is prolonged and is not cured with this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep, and is pressing on the bone, or the hard parts, or ligaments; treat it with the treatment of fistula, as we have said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaris is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or perhaps it arises on other fingers; and when it becomes old and is neglected, a bad abscess develops, festering and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps even entirely consumes it; and the erosion reaches the bone, causing fetid pain, and the finger swells, and its color is black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the division, and the treatment is ineffective, you must cut away all the remaining excess of the nail with a sharp knife, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, beginning to prick and wound it, then you must place a spatula underneath the nail that is piercing the flesh and lift it upwards, and carefully and gently cut the flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the erosion is in the bone, cut it and remove it, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger is corrupt, cut it off at the joint, as previously stated, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is bruised, and swollen, and it feels great pain, you must heal it first; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula, cutting across, and beware that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel great pain; and if it does happen, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the sore hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The finger growths that arise in some people's hands by chance are entirely fleshy, or sometimes contain bones, and sometimes have a nail. Some arise at the base of the joint, or the growth is in certain parts of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those that grow on any part of the finger do not move, and those that grow at the finger joint sometimes do move. The cutting of the fleshy ones is gentle, in this manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow at the base of the joint are difficult to cure: avoid cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those that grow on the finger's back part, you should first cut the round flesh down to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joining together of the fingers comes from growth, or from the healing of a wound, or from a burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut the join so that the fingers return to their natural shapes. Then place between them soaked cloths or oiled bandages so they do not rejoin, or place between two thin lead sheets until the area is joined as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a joining occurs between any of the fingers and the palm, cut that join as is appropriate.
des vils	of the vile ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large, swollen, full of melancholy superfluities that appear on many parts of the body; and these appear more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Then you must give him some purging of the bile, and then bathe him with the basilikon.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut them and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you tie the vein and draw it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first, immerse the leg in very hot water until the thick blood is thinned, then bind the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one, or two, or three places with a wide cut, then raise and draw the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood flows out as the patient's strength can endure; and then tie it, and instruct him to eat foods that increase black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bathing when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the vein is done in this manner: shave the patient's leg if it has much hair, then put it in a bath, and immerse the leg in hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, then heat it by fire, and then cut it in the vein's direction from the top of the knee to the area below the ankle; then open the skin with a lancet, and scrape the vein from each side, until it is visible when touched; and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord; then put the scraper underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then hang it gently on a lancet; then cut it in another place above the three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears; then raise it with the scraper, as you did before, and hang it on another lancet, as you did before; then cut another incision, or several if you need them; then raise it, and cut it at the toe of the foot, then pull and raise it to the second incision; then pull it from incision to incision until it comes out entirely, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and raise it, then put a needle with a strong double thread, and tie it and pull it, and put a scraper underneath, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, because if it cuts, it cannot be pulled or raised, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have pulled it all out, put wet wool in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted, twisted, and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it twistingly, but do not cut it; and pull it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which you cut the vein is curved, and not sharp, so that it does not cut the vein; and it is of a large curve, because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is embedded in legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and perhaps it arises elsewhere than in legs, and this happens from the decay that comes from under the skin, as it comes from within the body of serpents and worms, embedded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes to the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head appears, you must wrap around a piece of lead of one and a half to two ounces, and the knot, and leave the lead hanging on the leg, and every time it emerges at the end, wrap it around the lead and the knot; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root until it is all out; for if you cut it, it will return into the flesh, and cause abscess and decay at the place, and a bad illness; for which reason it is necessary to treat it little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when treated, is five palms long, or ten, and a man came to me, from whom it emerged ten palms long, and when you cut it, put one iron or hole, and pierce it to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and the matter within is emptied, and medicaments are administered to the place to prevent any decay, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and many holes emerge from it, and from which it springs; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called "bull's disease" in our land, because it often happens to bulls, and it is a small worm that arises between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body, going up and down, and one feels it clearly moving from limb to limb, until it pierces the skin where it goes, and emerges; and it is caused by the corruption of certain humors, like worms, serpents, leeches, and ascarides in the belly; and one fears its malice, for when it travels through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it reaches the eye, perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you want to treat and extract it, it can only be done when it is visible: you must therefore tie the area above and below with a strong bandage tightly, then cut over it and pull it out; and if the worm is deep within the flesh, and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire above, until it is charred; and the greatest harm it causes is that it can damage the eye, as we have said; and if you see it approaching the eye on the head, press the eyebrow firmly below it, then cut over it and pull it out; and the patient must use body cleansing and medicines that dissolve the bad rotten humors, and refrain from foods that cause decay.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes to certain limbs, and can move from limb to limb; and I have seen this, as I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and a little after, I saw it rise like a worm on her shoulder, more quickly than anything, like quick silver when it runs from one place to another; the pain left that place and settled in her shoulder, and then a little after ran throughout her body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it repeatedly circled around her body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from limb to limb like that, for I had never seen this illness in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many that had experienced pain moving from one place to another, but I had never seen it like I saw it in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins exposed, and because of that the windiness appeared constrained; and it does not appear according to this reasoning in those who are fleshy, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
