Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to cure this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears as we have said, then apply leeches above and below quickly, and then cut as far as the constrained windiness in the place comes out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with things that expel windiness, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places on the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are those with large points, and small, and feathered, and soldered; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that strikes any limb strikes in two ways: either in a principal member, such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it strikes then in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you after, appear to you: then it is necessary that you abstain from the extraction of this arrow, for death follows in many ways; and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when the arrow strikes it and pierces the bone, and the surface of the brain bursts, are: when there is scotoma and swelling and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of thought, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is a discharge of blood from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there comes from the wound a white moisture like pus, and there is also an outburst of burnt flesh; and if these signs appear, refrain from treatment and pull the arrow out if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood flows, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting occur: then know without doubt that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that wounds the lungs are that frothy blood flows from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the breast, it is next to the small ribs; and it throws out great blood and great pain and sighs; and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps some undigested food comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly, and bits of straw come out through the intestines, there is no hope for treatment, nor for the removal of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine flows out, and the patient feels intense pain, know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, shoulder blade, spine of the back, arms, thighs, and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck his tear duct at the base of his nose: I tried it, and removed it from the other side, under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I removed an arrow that struck the fat of the eye under the eyelid, and the arrow was embedded, and I could only reach its point towards the shaft, and the arrow was large, from a Turkish bow, with no feathers; the man was healed, and no bad accident happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with feathers: I separated the chin, and carefully removed it until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I removed an arrow from a man, which had struck his abdomen, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut around the arrow, and extracted it, and removed it completely, and he had no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And I saw a man whose arrow struck his back, and the wound was closed over; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural dispositions, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural activities.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, whom an arrow struck in his face, and the wound was closed; and it remained like that without suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I removed an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had struck him in the middle of his nose, and was slightly angled to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to treat him after it had been lodged there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a very thin probe, and felt nothing; and he felt a prick and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I put an attracting and digesting plaster on the area, so that it wouldn't swell; and the arrowhead's position became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the plaster on for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained like that for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose one day; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a sharp, corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it opened up, and I probed it, and felt the arrowhead moving in the area; then I added more of that sharp medicine to the opening of the wound, until the arrowhead became clearly visible; and the healing process lasted for about four months, and then the wound enlarged enough that I inserted pliers, and moved it from side to side, but it wouldn't come out; then I continued to refine and invent various instruments, until I used pliers well-crafted, according to what their form will be at the end of this chapter, so that I extracted it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it nonetheless, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the nature of extracting some arrows, so that you should apply your treatment to what I have not said, for the book cannot encompass everything; but a wise master, comparing a small thing with a greater one, and concerning himself with what is present and lacking, finds new work and new instruments, in response to the unusual things which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the limbs where they are lodged except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or through another place; and the one that exits through the place where it entered is an arrow that entered fleshy areas, and sometimes exits immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not exit immediately, leave it until the surrounding flesh is softened and the exit is eased; and if it is lodged in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it each day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce around it with a very fine drill, until the surrounding area is enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the symptoms that I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not extract it, but leave it until it is equal [in size] after some days, for if the arrow reaches this point, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone, and does not reach the point of no return, and the patient remains for several days without bad symptoms, then plan for its removal.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot come out, apply drills around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in a part of the body where it cannot be seen, search for it all around; and if you feel it, remove it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot, because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, cut it, so that the wound is large; and extract the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has hooks by which it is held, remove the flesh that is stuck to the two sides of the arrow as far as you can, then break or bend the arrow's hooks until you can remove it; and take care not to break the arrow, so that you can remove it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it at once, leave it until the surrounding area is rotten, then remove it, because extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you hesitant, use the treatment mentioned in that chapter; and avoid cutting the nerve and vein, and plan how you can safely remove the arrow, quickly or slowly, gently or firmly; and place the patient in the same position he was in when the arrow entered, because this is the most important aid, and if you cannot, place it according to the signs that are shown.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow comes from another direction, or some part of it is visible, or the skin is swollen where it is seen or felt clearly, then cut there, until the pincers can grasp it, and then pull it out: it will come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for a while, and then start pulling again until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, use the entire shaft; and if the shaft has fallen, and you want to apply thrusting, use a pointed instrument so that the arrowhead enters the instrument's tip; then thrust it out, and if the arrow is broken, apply an instrument with an entering point to aid extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is lodged in the buttocks, or the belly, or the bladder, or the ribs, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut above it, cut there; and be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, then pull it out, and then suture the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers with which arrows are pulled out is similar to a bird's beak, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many varieties: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrow-head is also like the feather of a bird, for pushing against the tip of the arrow, as here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and for holding is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which one bleeds, there are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen in the head.  That is to say: two arteries located behind the ears, which are called the "two herbeches"; and the two arteries that are in the two apparent temples; and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspirates"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the root of the nose; and the two veins that are in the neck; and the two veins located on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and two veins located beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the medial is called "faste", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and is above the elbow, and is the one from which one bleeds, which is clearly visible on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the ulnar and radial, and has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the bend of the wrist on the left side, and the second is the saphenous that is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Bleeding the veins behind the ears helps with chronic colds, and headaches; and the method of bleeding, as I tell you, is this: you raise the head of the sick person, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then have the sick person tighten their neck with a bandage, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places on the head: then grasp them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, then press firmly; then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein to the bone; then lift your hand all the way up the vein, and cut both the skin and the vein with two cuts through, and let the blood flow as much as you want; then bind and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already discussed incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Bleeding the two arteries in the temples is good for chronic, severe headaches, and persistent eye inflammation, and for severe eye pain; and the method of bleeding is as I describe: have the patient tighten their neck until the two veins are clearly visible; feel the pulse under your finger, then press firmly; then lift the head of the vein upwards with your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and cut it, as you did with the other two veins, and let the blood flow as needed; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on; then bandage firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already discussed their cutting and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Bleeding the vein of the forehead is as good as bleeding the cephalic vein for chronic facial ailments, headaches, and redness; and the method is that the patient tightens their neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called a "cutter," of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and strike it with your hand, or another object, and let the blood flow according to the amount you want; then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed; and sometimes it is treated with a wide-flamed fire.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame should not be too sharp; and bleed across, for the bone is close, and perhaps the flame will break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Bleeding the two veins located in the tear ducts helps the eyes, and for scabies, and redness, and inflammation in the eye, and facial ailments; and the method for their bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck by twisting with a bandage, as before; then bleed, and let the bleeding be crosswise, a bit of the flame length, a bit wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is thin, perhaps it will break; then make the blood flow as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Bleeding the vein in the nose is good for gout, and for sudden madness, and for facial ailments, like migraines and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old; and the method for the bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck, then holds their nose with your left hand, and take a thin, long flame, and insert it in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein is not clearly seen there, and the blood will now start to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the flame's form:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Bleeding the two veins in the groin helps with tightness in the groin, and the beginning of illness, and many ailments, and for impetigo, and for sores, and for herpes, and for ulcers; and the method for the bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck from underneath, as we have said; and let the master be above the patient's head, and the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein lengthwise a bit wide, then draw blood moderately, or as much as needed; then do the same to the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and moderately constrict both veins so the patient does not suffocate; and leave it until morning, for the wound to heal.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding the veins on the upper lip helps with sores in the mouth, and with gum corruption, and lip cracks, and nose and throat ailments.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the method for the bleeding is to have the patient sit before you, and tighten their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look for the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which are recognized by being dark, and by the small dark veins around them: then cut both of them, and if you don't recognize them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and likewise do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is one and the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleeding the veins under the tongue helps after bleeding the cephalic vein, and it is for constrictions of the throat, and ailments of the eye, and mouth ailments; and the method of bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and you lift their tongue, and look under each side for a dark vein: then bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep, for the arteries are underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm, which are commonly bled, are bled according to two methods: either by pricking with a wide, sharp lancet, or with a thin, lancet-like one, called "anesil"; and they are wide or thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the lancet is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is useful for opening veins full of thick, visible blood, and that contain thick and troubled blood; and that is the shape of the olive-shaped lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and slender, and is for bleeding thin veins, where there is thin, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	Bleeding from the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the physician to bleed wisely, and that he be wary of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, it must be stopped, as I have said; and the lancet should not be piercing, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica vein does not appear clearly, you must bind it, and change to another; or you seek some branch from it, or you bleed from a vein in the middle of the arm: it appears clearly; and cut it with a knife-like lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place for the bleeding, you must first tie the arm, touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place with a pen, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a knife-like lancet; and be careful that you do not strike the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is of the artery: stop it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it gushing up like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; tie the arm, and leave it like that, and do not move it the patient; and let him be careful, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it overwhelms you, and the medicine is not present, cut the artery if it appears, for its head retracts; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a fig-tree bark, and split it, and take one half and tie it on well until the next day; if the blood stops, it is good; if not, treat it, as we have said, with the powders that stop blood; and the stopping of it is not difficult in many cases due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the bandage of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Bleeding from the vein in the middle helps it to draw blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful of the nerve that is below, and if he cuts too deep and finds the nerve, it swells and the patient's condition worsens, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men because of its thinness, you should then bleed it with a knife; and protect the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, slit it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	Bleeding from the cephalic vein helps, drawing blood from the head and aiding the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed by puncturing the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because it is the safest of all the veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery below it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, one must seek the easiest place, and it does no harm if one fails the first time, and one tries again; and perhaps the place swells in some people the first time one fails, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is only administered to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are on the arm: namely, the cephalic, the basilic, and the median cubital; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring on an empty stomach, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding administered for illnesses has no set time, but only when needed, by day or by night, at all hours and times; and one should not bleed children until fourteen years old, nor women pregnant except from the fourth month to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people over sixty years should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in any way, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a gentle clyster if they have retained much waste, so that the veins do not draw superfluous and harmful impurities from the intestines to the main limbs; and do not bleed those who are overly full of food, or who are drunk, as long as they are affected, or those who are hydrops; and one should avoid bleeding after a colic attack, vomiting, or diarrhea, and multiple sexual activity, and labor, and fatigue, and fasting, and anything that weakens the entire body or spirit; then subtilize the humors if the blood is thick, by food and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then enter a bath, if nothing forbids it, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein on the arm near the elbow, as we said; and guard against labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things on that day; and be at peace and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than the one being bled, and the bleeder rub the arm two or three times, then tie the bandage moderately, for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow; and then the bleeder rubs the place with their hands until the veins swell and are felt; then the bleeder moistens the blade with a bit of old oil, then place their left hand's finger on the vein below the place where they want to bleed, so that the vein does not break and fail when the blade strikes.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like cords when bleeding, and some that are full of wind, so that when the blade is placed on them, it recoils, and the vein will not open, and so it is with those; and if it opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, so the bleeder must be careful about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, start again a little below or above that spot, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen, and the patient is afraid, let it be for a day or two, and do not tie the arm: perhaps a hot abscess will result; do not enter a bath, then resume the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly, and you fear it will not release as much blood as desired, then strike the blade straight into that same opening, and open it slightly above or below, before the place becomes swollen; because this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not resume the bleeding, and apply a bit of oil-soaked linen, for it lightens the blood's flow and the linen is gentler on the area than oil; and thus apply oil-soaked linen to every bleeding when you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same effect is achieved with herbs and poultices, when applied to the area; it will subtilize the blood and separate it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess arises, which happens often, especially when it has not been bled frequently or when the opening of the vein is small, hurry and apply a sponge moistened with hot water and salt to the area, and compress it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if some discoloration or greenness remains in the area after a few days, it will not hurt; and if you wish, apply something made from aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess or appearance occurs during bleeding from the basilica vein: therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the area soft to the touch, that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything we have mentioned, for perhaps arterial blood will flow; but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of their strength and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thinned; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for someone who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, make a larger wound, and let the incisions be wide; and for someone who is weak, do the opposite, and let them be bled little and often, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood flow and nerve damage, and it is better than bleeding from long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for someone whose body weakens during bloodletting, give them bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are heated, draw blood three or four times. And if they are of a cold complexion, give them bread soaked in syrup of grape must, or in syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup, before the bloodletting.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if they faint during bloodletting, after the outflow of much blood, they should drink broth of meat and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to empty his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he be bled little by little, according to the amount of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to empty their arm after the first bloodletting, and they have a strong body, should bleed seven hours after the first bloodletting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another part, should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and causes fever; so it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and enlarge the opening until it bleeds freely; and after you have observed all the conditions of bloodletting, and place your hand on their pulse when they bleed, so that death does not come in place of fainting, and this happens many times when the bloodletter is negligent; and it is not appropriate when you wish to untie the arm and make blood flow the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly on it; nor if it is bent, that they extend the arm quickly, for this would be bad; but allow it to bleed the second time; or you prick it with the tip of the firebrand, so that the blood that has solidified in the opening of the vein flows forcefully, and place a small amount of salt dissolved in water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is bled instead of the vein in the head, because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bloodletting is that the patient puts their hand in warm water until the vein is red; then it is bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then bleed through it directly, not broadly or lengthwise; and let the opening be wide, and let it be bled close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not return the hand to warm water, for it is put more in winter than in summer; and bloodletting from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are neither arteries nor nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding from the vein on the back of the right hand is good for all liver illnesses, and this is the method: restrain the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein is swollen, so that it is visible; and if you bleed through it, and if you cut it completely through, it will not hurt; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath, all bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as you need, put oil and wax over the vein to quickly close it, and do the same with each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding from the vein in the left hand is good for mice-related illnesses, and do everything just as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bleeding from the vein of the *sophene* (likely a specific anatomical location) is good for all illnesses below the body, such as illnesses of the stomach, and retention of fluids, and illnesses of the kidneys, thighs, and older legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the method for this bleeding is that the patient places their foot in hot water, and rubs the vein until it swells, and tie above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot, there goes a lot of blood; bleed then at the wider vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed from the vein on the foot, be careful of the nerves below, and bleed through it as if cutting; and let the flame be near.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, return the foot to the water, and allow the vein to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the bleeding fails the first time, begin again a little higher, for the place is salty; and do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the *sophene* of the other foot likewise.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the thigh, and its bleeding is good for hip pain, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the method of its bleeding is that the patient enters the bath, and squeezes above the ankle with four fingers by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not appear; and if it appears, bleed it in every way you can, and by crossing; and it is better to cut it, for the place is safe, and it is very easily pierced by the hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, bleed any vein that appears on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and be wary of the nerves; and make as much blood flow as you want, and then loosen the bandage, and put cotton on and bind it; it is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cuppings.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping is made of horns, or of bronze, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without striking is in two ways: either with fire, or without fire; and cupping done by striking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is at the top of the head; and another in the middle of the neck; and two others on the two sides of the neck; and the cup under the chin; and the cup on the two shoulders; and the cup on the buttocks; and the cups between the two arms; and the cups on the two legs; and the cups on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw any blood, except for the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken one, as one does with venesection; and it is not necessary that it be administered, either with or without fire, in any illness arising from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if cupping is necessary for illnesses, or for custom, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at all times; for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have the tongue swollen, and spit blood; and there are some who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order cupping after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the temple helps the heaviness of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this cupping is in place of bloodletting from the cephalic vein, and it is not necessary that those of cold complexion use it, or those who have a cold, for this does them much harm; and therefore it is not necessary that the elderly use it, nor those who have cold ailments in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cup a little lower, due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping in the neck is in place of bloodletting from the head and from the basilary vein, and therefore it is useful for tightness of the breast, and for a slit in the bronchial passage, and for coughs, and for fullness; and it should be applied lightly, for if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness in the stomach and in the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in place of bloodletting from the basilary vein; and you should instruct the person that when applying it, they should press their hand firmly so that they do not cut the artery, and no bleeding occurs.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping under the chin is good for mouth ailments, and for gum corruption, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in place of bloodletting from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is good for ailments that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cupping on the elbows is as good as bloodletting from the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the person not to strike too deep, for the area is bare of flesh and has nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for ailments underneath, and it is necessary that the cupping be large, and be of brass, so that it can draw well; and perhaps if it were small, it would break; and it causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping on the legs draws blood openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the kidneys, and the bladder, and the intestines, and draw out the flowers; and are in place of the two soles, and the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause pallor in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying a cupping is to first make it empty, and suck gently, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from this until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then release, and replace the cupping glasses, and be careful in the disposition of the body, because there are those who have thick flesh and thin skin: then it is necessary to strike only once, and make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin the thick blood's path.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out little blood by little, one strike is enough.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we recommence often; and if the blood is thick, strike deep, and the outcome is that the heart is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with thick skin and narrow pores to anoint the cupping places with an aperitive and dissolvent oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter-tasting oil, or balsam oil, or dill oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being treated has tender skin and wide pores, no oil should be put on, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or blackberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them use willow bark or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those with thick superfluities should use old wine, or spring water, or dill or chamomile decoctions, or other similar things; and one should not be cupped with a cupping glass before or during a bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and one should not sleep after cupping, and one needs to wash oneself when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the person being treated is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; then they should take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, and lettuce with oil, and similar things; and let them eat less, and rabbit and hare meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and middling scented wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat small rabbits, and small birds and pigeons; and the day they are to be cupped, they should drink more than eat; and sometimes one must give some men a little triacle or nutmeg before or after cupping, to strengthen the main limbs; and let the blood be thinned, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are placed without causing injury are those placed on the liver, the spleen, gout, the belly, the gut, the kidneys and the hip, for these members do not tolerate being struck on them, and one does not do it other than to attract blood from one member to another, as we place them on the breasts when the nipple is inflamed; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put cupping glasses on the belly and the gut to reduce the member; and it removes pain, when there is obstruction or stone, so it removes by its attractive power perhaps the obstruction, or removes the stone from its place; and so it does when it is placed on the liver and the spleen when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty only to suck; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes full of lukewarm water, as in illnesses of the pleura, and in such a way that one fills the cupping glass with only warm water, or with water in which one has boiled suitable herbs for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should have two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have one small hole near the middle, as for pushing a needle, and be of bronze, soft beforehand so that it does not hurt the patient when placing it on the member; and have a crosswise rod of bronze or iron in the middle, to place a lit candle, and be both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the elderly, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must put this cupping glass on the member like this: take the candle of wax or a wick, and place it in the middle of the cupping glass through the rod that is in the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wants, the vapor will go out, and one removes the cupping glass; and one takes the wick as before, and starts again often, if you need to.
