En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass, then, that is administered in a pleurisy illness, with water only, there is no rod or hole, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and is placed on the member simply; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are only administered to members where cupping glasses cannot be placed due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, such as the toe or nose, and others similar; and the quality of use is that when you find leeches that are in clear, fresh water without injury, take them; and put them in fresh water for a night, until they are full, and have nothing in their stomachs; and then be bled from a vein and from a cupping glass, and rub the member until it is red, and place the leeches; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where one can place a cupping glass, then do so, for this is very helpful afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the place with ease, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the place bleeds too much after the leeches have left, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water and apply, so that the blood is stopped; and if the blood is multiplied, then apply ground vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until it is stopped; or you put half a handful of shelled beans on the place, and leave them until they are burned to the place, it will now stop; and if you need more, then take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches do not want to take hold, rub the place with fresh blood, or you stick a needle into it until blood comes out, and then place them on it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they take hold; and when you want them to drop off, then sprinkle a little ground alum and salt, or ashes, on it, and they will fall off now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish men disdain this chapter, as if they had never seen any of the ancient books, nor read a letter from them; and for this reason, the science is strange in our land, for I have never found any good one; and I know nothing about it except through the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have learned its science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have now described in this chapter what is contained within, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we state in the prologue of this book the summary of the words and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding, and stays on the truth, so that those who have experience know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs to someone, you must hasten to bleed the patient on both sides, if nothing prevents you from doing so, such as weakness of the body, or being a child, or an elder; or if the weather is not too hot or too cold; and avoid cold foods, that is to say cold meats, and the flesh of birds and young deer, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill the body too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, so that you do not fear a hot abscess or the spreading of matter to the limb; thus, the patient should return to the first regimen they have been using.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide substantial nourishment, or which have viscosity, such as boiled wheat in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the fracture heals more quickly and better.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot properly heal or unite according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those who are too young, such as the bones of small children; but there is no cure; hold the broken bone in large splints that hold and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and do not neglect their care, and for this, they must be nourished with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go across, and others lengthwise, like the edge of a writing pen.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with a wound, and fractures with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each kind there is its own device and proper instrument in restoration, according to what the memory brings to its place; and a fracture of the bone is known by its twisted place, and is clearly revealed by a defect, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound on touching, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move it by hand, but apply the medicines that come after, and then gently hold it steady.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that fractures that go across, and where the two parts are separated, they must be brought to equal points, lest a hot abscess come; and if a hot abscess comes, leave it for a while until the abscess is calmed; then put it back in place as easily and wisely as you can, and know that the restoration is easier when there are whole pieces than when there are broken pieces; then hold it steady, as it should be done later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is a hand or foot, or hold it with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, bring all additions back into their places as easily as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain; and carefully join the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it carefully with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: then straighten it nicely, and do not hold it too tightly, nor press it as those do who cause a hot abscess and contraction in the limb with their work, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, properly restrain the patient so that he does not move it, neither while waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and carefully ensure that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not properly in place, and it must be put into such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that it is placed straight, so that no twisting occurs when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in size and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar parts: soft and fine linen cloths must be wrapped around them; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: a wide and firm bandage must be wrapped around them, for the wide bandage encompasses the entire large limb and tightens it equally on all sides so that there is no unevenness; then tie around light padding, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the entire bandage, then go above the break and tighten it less, so that the break then moves the break slightly; and soften the bandage little by little, until you take a large part of the sound area, then take another bandage and turn it around the broken area again; then go again to the area below the break and tighten it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first book above; then place linen padding or cloths between the bandages, until it is all even, then tie everything over a bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something soothing for abscesses that is warm and that removes the swelling, and leave it this way for several days; then bind on your splints, and let them be half the width of a skillfully cut cane, or of the wood from which planks are made, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint placed over the break be a little thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as necessary for the limb, whether small or large; then tighten the splints as you did in the first book, then tie over them a suitable thread, as in the first book over the break; tighter at the top, gradually looser; and the thread must be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bandages with twisted linen rope, and that is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not necessary that there be less than a finger's width of space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the edges of the splints after tightening in healthy areas, place linen padding or wool cloth under them so that he is not injured.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind splints to all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to apply splints immediately but only after 5 or 7 days, or more, depending on the safety of a hot abscess arising; and see here the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: and it is that you take flour that remains on the mill walls, and mix it with abundance of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of plaster restoring fractures in many ways, and especially to women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster restoring fracture, dislocation, and twisting: take 3 drachms of saffron, and of ladani, and enule, and asafetida, and gum arabic, and mugat, all in quantity of 10 drachms; myrrh and aloes, each 5 drachms; and alechil 9 drachms; and make it into powder, and mix it with abundance of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster that is good for twisting: take mugat and vismalve, each 10 drachms; myrrh and aloes, each 9 drachms; acaice 6 drachms; Armenian bole 10 drachms, and grind well, and mix with water or abundance of egg, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another plaster for joints and bones separated from their place, and calms the pain that comes, and the bone’s use, and the fracture: take new wool, and soak it in oil and cooked oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for calming a hot abscess, and properly relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and leaves of wild poppy, and grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another plaster for the restoration of broken bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, chickpea flour, each a part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another plaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mallow, and flaxseed, balm, melilot, and plantain, and violet and chamomile flowers, of all an equal part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore strength anything but a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else besides, and says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should put on a broken limb, for restoration, slightly warm dry things, such as myrrh, aloes, frankincense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another kind of plaster which is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and chopped human hair, or bird feathers, and mallow, and silphium equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove it a little later, and watch if the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, do not remove it for many days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and remove it, and take the plaster away immediately; and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and apply it to the area, until the itching ceases, and the pain is relieved; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, moistened in water or rose-colored oil, and bandage it for a night, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then begin the gentle binding again, with a little plaster, and do not bind it so tightly as before; and continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess, redness, pain, and swelling have all been removed, and you need a plaster and bandage, then start again, as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing from what we have said happens to the limb, then do not unbind it until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what you see, until the fracture heals, and the flesh approaches; then bind it tighter than before, and increase its nourishment, as I said before; and if you see the area drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; then moisten it with warm soft water every time you unbind it, and that should be every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; by this work, then, the limb's nourishment comes quickly, and amends quickly what foolish surgeons do, who restore the limb incorrectly: it is bad, and it is a fearful work, and I see nothing else than to leave it and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many types of fractures exist, with diverse forms and distinct causes; for there are fractures caused by a sword blow, and the blow removes the entire bone, down to the soft tissue beneath the bone, as a hatchet or a piece of wood does; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "hatchet fracture.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone in a piercing manner, and this type of fracture is called "complete"; and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blunt impact, or a fissure, or a blow from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar instances.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches the tissue beneath the bone, or which is on the surface of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there are wounds that are notched in the bone as thin as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "hairline"; and if the wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and forces a piece of bone inward, and the place is split, as when blacksmiths hit their cauldrons, so the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to subjects who have soft or moist bones, such as a child's head; and happens with all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated, as if they are stars; and I will discuss this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the pull on them, and the examination with probes, and by the corrupt flesh on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is recognized because when the bone has been uncovered, and you rub on it, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, take heed of the patient's accidents, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, loss of consciousness, extension, paleness, acute fever, and the eyes turning white and red, and other similar things in various dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a dreadful accident, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the tissue under the bone is corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part like this: and you must take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in every way you can, and over the wound's surface gently as much as you can, and if a discharge of blood comes when uncovering the bone, or a hot abscess, help with what is needed, and you must fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and be sure that the discharge of blood has stopped; then start removing the bone around it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is to cut tightly beforehand, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then add another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron; and work lightly, so you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, then you must pierce it around, before you apply cuts with drills, not deep enough that they pierce the bone of the skull, and there should be a margin or circle over the point, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you should have several of them, so that each one comes to its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for all the surfaces; and this is the shape of the three methods of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place a drill on the bone, and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then reposition the drill elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone with your hand, or with any of the tools you have, such as pliers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, you must remove the remaining piece of bone using any other tool similar to a chisel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other chisels; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen said, which is safer; and he praised it very much, and that is his statement.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you expose a part of the bone, where the fracture is apparent, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this lenticular chisel, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And it does not cut on one side, and its part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet, so that you cut the bone all around, and be very careful of the tissue that is underneath; if it is stuck to the bone, remove it gently, for it is removed well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through to the tissue, and the bone is only broken on the surface, and there are small pieces, you must scrape away that roughness and remove the scales with a delicate scraper of which you must have various sizes, to apply the most suitable one to each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use large scrapers first, and then finer ones, and do not stop until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other cuts and subtle fractures, you must apply the cause according to its direction; and this is something not easily understood by one who has not devoted study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the surface is exposed, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as possible so you do not irritate the surface, then apply another bandage over it, and do not bind it too tightly, only so that it holds the wound; and leave it thus for one or two days, until the inflamed abscess is calmed, then remove it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make powder from these things, and place it on the wound, and frequently apply healing medicines without causing inflammation; and be sure that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave ointment there, or allow pus to collect, for when pus gathers on the brain tissue, it will corrupt and fester, and cause the patient great harm; because when you put something corrosive on the surface, it will burn from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be warned, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly dangerous.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blackening does not occur except because of the medicine applied, that it may have such a power, you must take a portion of honey, and three portions of rose oil and glue a cloth, and place it over the surface; then treat it with the necessary treatments until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two upper parts of the nose are broken, or one of them alone, for they are two bones; and the one underneath is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is bruised or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must place your little finger or the small opening of the nose, and place the broken part of the nose against your index finger, and the other part out back, until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, you must place it equal to the head of a slightly thick reed.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, repeat the same process, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscess has subsided, then place strips of linen cloth on the head of the nose, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the strips be so large that they fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers said that one should moisten the strips in butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but they should be moistened in a mixture of egg white and flour powder; then leave the strip, until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one places goose feathers in the nose in place of strips, and places a soft cloth around them, and the fracture remains stable, and the patient breathes through them; now do whatever you want.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a boil arises in the nose while you are working on it, put a plaster or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a little diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil does not arise, apply a plaster externally, made of crushed flaxseed and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then place light cloths over it, and do not bind the nose; and if the nose fracture is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with appropriate instruments, then suture the wound, and treat it with substances that are good for closing flesh wounds and bonding, such as plasters and suitable ointments; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with strips, and place lead splints in it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken below, and there is no wound externally, and the fracture is only external, and is not broken in two, except for the projections inside, it is recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, put your right index finger in, and gently push the fractured part inward, and hold it steady with the other hand externally, and apply equal pressure.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two, it is necessary that you apply extension to both parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or are fractured, bind them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place a plaster on the fractured jaw, and put a double bandage over it; and place a large, well-made plaster, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it as firmly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, unbind it on the third day, and then return to the original state what has changed; and apply a plaster of mill powder with plenty of egg or flaxseed flour, after removing the bandage; and put light wool over the plaster, and if the plaster is effective and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times he is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, examine whether any piece of the bone has been detached; if necessary, carefully remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and nothing remains, close the wound if it is large, and apply appropriate plasters to promote healing until he is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times before, toward the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken forceps; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put the fracture straight with your fingers, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and make it as large as needed; and extend and lift the forceps, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceps out, because it has gone deep, it is necessary for the patient to lie often on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and the assistants push the shoulder down until the bone of the forceps is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, you must split it open; and pull the pieces out gently, and if the bone cannot join despite any effort, cut it with one of the incisors you have; but place this instrument under the forceps to protect its surface:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and be as wide as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two heads, as you see, and one wide, and the other narrow, as is the incision you made when you pulled the bones out; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, cauterize the wound, and if the incision is small, or you suspect a hot abscess, fill the wound with bandages and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, soak a bandage in rose oil and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and cuts, is to apply to the bone a plaster of mill powder and egg white, and place light cloths over it, and place a bolster under the armpit, if necessary; then take a very wide bandage, one palm wide, then place a double bandage over the cloths and plaster; then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the end of the bandage hangs down; and place the splint over the fracture, and tie the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the diseased armpit; and bind it from each part, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture in place, and you clearly see that the splint does not move over the broken bone, then check it daily, and when the binding loosens, tighten it; and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the armpit when they sleep, to raise the shoulder; this will ease the fracture of the shoulder by lifting the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, until 20 days; then renew the plaster, if you see that it is necessary, and tighten and leave it so until it is restored; and it is restored in the maximum of 28 days, and in less time in some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Often the shoulder breaks in a broad area or in the middle, and it is not clear where except by touch; then align it according to the fracture's shape and bring it back to its natural form, in every way you can; then put mill powder with egg white, and soft cloths, and place a double bandage over it; then place a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there are gaps under the splint in any part of the shoulder, fill those gaps with linen cloths, so that the splint lies evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the bandage daily; and whenever it loosens, tighten it, and put the splint back in place if it moves from its position, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is complete, untie it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that moves easily out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone is sticking out, and is right under the skin, then cut it open and remove it, and do as we said in the treatment of a hot abscess of the shoulder.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the pelvis
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The pelvis is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it is often broken on the outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it sinks downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of breath, and sickness, and perhaps vomits blood, and the skin appears broken open on the broken bone, and one can feel it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and carefully adjusts to all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place dressings and bandages over the delicate layer of salt, or another light substance, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it over the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage tightly around the back, and tighten it appropriately, and check the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, tighten it; and if it needs to be untied, because of a sore or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and remove the dressing, and address whatever has developed in terms of treatment; then replace the dressing, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs mainly occurs in the thick parts behind the back, and at the inside edge, and they only bend because they are frail; and one can easily feel this by examining the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the dressing, and bind it with a bandage, if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is leaning inward, the patient feels very great pain, and stabbing, just like a piercing, because the bone pierces the tissue; and breathes with difficulty, and coughs and vomits copious amounts of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients devoted much effort to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest a hot abscess appear, if it has not already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if one has appeared, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some among you say that cupping should be applied to the area, to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping will draw out superfluities to the place due to a disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some among you say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and one places tents between the ribs to uniformly apply the bandage, then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone piercing the flesh, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to cut open the area of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument beneath it to protect the surface; and then one should cut the bone, and pull lightly, and then stitch the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes, then place cloths soaked in rose oil on it; and treat the area as is appropriate for an abscess, and let it lie often on the affected side until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and it rarely bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then observe if you see their hands softened and swollen and lifeless, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many ways, and if they move them and feel them well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if he will be healed or not, observe if the feet are softened, and if the signs are as in the hands, and if windiness and involuntary discharge are present on the back; and when he is turned on his stomach, involuntary discharge occurs.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal: so do not labour in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not happen to him, the matter is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should look for a hot abscess, then apply rose oil or egg oil to the spine until it subsides; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is separated, it is necessary to cut over the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, and then treat it with a healing ointment until it is healed; and if the bone head is broken, which is called the 'head of the leg', put your left hand's finger on it, and bring it as equal as you can to the other hand, and then apply the plaster and the bandage if you need it; then bind it, and if there is a separated bone, split it open and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes the hip bone is fractured, and if it is, there is often a slight splintering at the head; and it splits lengthwise, and bends inward, and the patient feels pain and piercing at the site, and the area around the break swells up.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you should extend your hand upward, until you are over the fracture; and know what is the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is only at the head, then set that fracture in alignment, so that it is of natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or if it bends inward, make the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of that fracture becomes clear to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, place a plaster over it, then put a splint of wood or of leather over it, and bind the fracture, so that it does not move; and fill the area under the ribs, so that the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess comes there, do not touch it until the hot abscess is calmed, and put on what we have previously said; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as necessary, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the ribs and the head of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, it should be restored according to one of two methods: one of which is that you take a stick of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two bands to the two ends, and hang them upward, and place the patient on a seat; then place the broken arm on the stick, until it reaches the armpit, and have a bend of the stick in the middle, then hang it on some heavy object, or the attendant extends it downwards; then let the attendant place the fracture straight with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his crutch, and ties the arm to his neck, then instructs two attendants that one should hold that which is on top of the fracture in his hands, and the other hold underneath with all his strength, and extend each to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, tie a band below the fracture, and above the fracture, and let each of the attendants extend to his side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, you must place a medium band under the armpit, and another towards the ribs, under the fracture; and likewise if the fracture is towards the ribs, a light band should be placed gently, without effort, until the fracture is aligned in place, and towards the ribs; then align the fracture as it should, and hold it tight, if no inflamed abscess appears.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an inflamed abscess appears, do not hold it tight for seven days, and place moistened wool in oil and rose oil, until the inflamed abscess subsides; then hold it tight, and the manner of holding it tight is that you place a plaster over the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and place the cloth, and hold it tight on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in the position of the bone, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will not stay in place, use splints, and place over the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends beyond the fracture three inches on each side; then hold tight on the splints, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter concerning the fracture, more tightly and less as you move away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the splints, and the tightening, as we have said, at the time you reset the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave it untied until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the binding every three days, that itching or swelling does not appear in the area, or that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is aligned, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, do not loosen it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; and place one cushion full of equal wool under the shoulder; and check every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or the bindings do not soften; if it aligns by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is initially subtle, and as it begins to recover, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be recovered within forty days altogether; and then one should loosen it and administer baths and ointments to align the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and swollen, let it remain unloosened for 50 days or two months.
