de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fossils," of which one is small, and is the one that supports the thumb; and the other is large, and is the one that is beneath, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large fossil breaks, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fossil is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more serious than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small fossil that is broken, it should be gently stretched a little, and put straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large fossil, it must be held tighter; and stretch it over a cushion, and keep the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and a cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then the ministers should extend their arms to the part below the hand, or to a sling, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then the healer must put it straight, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breakage there are pieces, put each in its place, and if any are detached that hurt the heart, and you cannot restore them to their place, then cut through them and remove them, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breakage there is a wound, I have spoken about it in a separate chapter; therefore take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration, there arise hot abscesses, then glue a plaster of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, that it be neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the plaster over subtly, until the hot abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerate, and put on the plaster of powdered millstone with plenty of egg, then put on the splints, and let the splints of the breakage be stronger, and a little wider than the others; and know that there should be six splints or more, in various positions: whether the breakage be in one bone, or in two; and tighten more over the breakage than elsewhere, and gradually less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And observe the limb and the bandage after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must wash the limb with hot water until the itching is calmed; and let the limb rest, not too tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the binding, and if the bandages are softened and the bones separated, or something similar, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little, and leave it thus for several days, until the nourishment flows to it, and then bind it more tightly.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happens to the patient, do not unbind it for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or, in conclusion, then the patient should hang their hands on their neck, and their necks should be even, and avoid movement and fidgeting, and sleep on their back; and know that this fracture is restored in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and the fingers there are few fractures, and there is mostly only bending many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient should sit cross-legged, and sit upright in front of them equally; then place their hand on a flat surface, and the attendants should straighten the broken bones and place them even, until they are properly joined; and apply the plaster and bandages, if no abscess is present, then place a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the inside of the palm, make a sling of cloth and instruct the patient to hold it to the fractured palm; and then wrap it with a long bandage, and the splint should be soft leather as large as the palm of the hand, and wrap it as required.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you should place one splint on top and another beneath the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it entirely around the hand, and tie the bandage between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, place it straight as required; and wrap it with the palm, and if you wish, place a small straight splint to raise the fracture and keep it still; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index finger or one of the others, place it straight and bind it with the healthy finger next to it; or tie them all together in a hold, as you see fit, or place a splint, as in the thumb; and be careful in the restoration and in the treatment of a hot abscess, and treat whatever comes up as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the fractured thigh.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often fractured, and it is clearly seen when it is turned forward and backward; and the restoration is done by tying one bandage over the fracture, and another underneath.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each attendant extends their bandage equally to their side; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, one bandage should be towards the groin, and the other bandage beneath the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then one bandage should be next to the knee, and the other extension downwards; then the attendant should place the bone straight with their two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster and bind it, if no abscess comes there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside then return to your work and your treatment; the binding is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap over the fracture one hard bandage doubled in two or three, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so the heel comes to the root of the hip, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee underneath, and have the thread's end above; then turn the bandage over the leg and over the thigh, then put strips over the fracture, and put a strip over the leg bone; then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the tightening equal, then begin to bind tightly three or four turns over the fracture; and as you go higher above the fracture, tighten less; then tie the two ends of the thread you put between the leg and the thigh, and bind three strips that are above, then go back below to the thread's end, until you come next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, so that no abscess or swelling or similar thing comes there.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, untie it, and correct what comes there, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it should be removed, if possible; and if not possible, it is necessary to split the place and pull force; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that strips are put on it, as in the shoulder and the arm; however, in the restoration done this way, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 40 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversities of the temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a fissure, or a hole, and it happens in every wound, both with and without a wound, and this is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by placing the fractured parts together, as much as possible; then, apply the plaster, and put a round splint if needed, and bind it as appropriate, then consider all the procedures we have described for other fractures, such as inflamed abscesses and similar things; provide the necessary treatment for each condition until healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one called 'tibia' and the other 'fibula'; and fractures happen in the same way as in the arm, and therefore the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the procedures are the same.  And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the smaller bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the larger bone is broken, great pain is felt, and it is clearly seen; and it turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer extension, and put it straight, and bind the splints evenly; however, if the fracture is severe, and there are multiple pieces, the extension should be gentler and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of wooden splints that support the leg on either side, and are the length of the leg from the knee down; then wrap two bandages over and under, and tie them in the middle as well, and with this binding the leg will not deviate to the right or left, and thus it is well done; and some administer one splint the length of the leg, also of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is done properly in a fracture where there is a wound; and move the leg each day to see if there is a hot abscess or other mishap; treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but fractures sometimes occur in the bones of the foot and the toes, and there is no injury other than a breaking into multiple fragments.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping, place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they were about to walk, and then place your foot on theirs, over the place where the bones are raised, and press them until they return to their position; then apply a plaster and bandages, and put a small board with two flat sides beneath the sole of the foot, and then wrap the foot with bandages, along with other materials you require.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are fractured, repair them as we described for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the fractured toe, slightly wider; then put the board under the foot as previously mentioned, and wrap it securely; and if there are two, three, or more fractured toes, place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in one linen bandage, and secure the board underneath the foot; and let the splint be positioned over the top of the board, so that it supports the sole of the foot well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have already stated; and treat each accident as appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the forearm
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's pelvic bone is fractured, place her in a reclining position, then incline her towards the back, and support her from behind; then let the attendant fill the woman's pelvic area with cotton, putting in as much as a fist; then lift the woman up, and gradually raise her back, and the cotton will rise until it reaches the opening of her pelvis, and the bone will return with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and continue this way for seven days or so: the fracture will be repaired, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a straw to the opening, and place the entire bladder in her pelvis; then blow into the straw forcefully, so that the bladder fills with air: the fracture will return to its position; then fill it with cotton and leave it thus for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the forearm bone of a man or woman is fractured, treat it as we have described for the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who diligently study and practice according to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies, in various dispositions, the correct path of restoration: understand it therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a fractured penis, take a goose's neck and place it on the penis; then wrap it with cloths and leave it for three days or thereabouts, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one with a fracture and a wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, that it be healed promptly, as the treatments we have described testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then seal it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then resume restoring the fracture at that same hour, or on that same day, if no painful abscess develops.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a painful abscess develops, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess subsides, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the exposed flesh, you must gently set it in place with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for aligning it with your hands, then use this instrument, which is made of iron, seven or eight inches long, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this, the smith needs to forge three or four, according to what is needed for each fracture treatment; and it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend when applying pressure to the limb during your work, and it should be pointed at the front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," so that the curved part must be placed over the head of the exposed bone; and it is put in place at once, so that it returns to its proper position, and be equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument can have purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, whether a scalpel or a saw, to the best of your ability; then remove what remains of the bone's roughness and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So do this until it is in its place, then soak a cloth in black astringent wine, and properly, if it is in the summer; and do not put a plaster or anything else with oil on the wound, lest it cause rot and corruption; then administer poultices when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the surrounding tissue according to the size of the wound, and carefully ensure that the wound is not constricted by the fracture; and many fools have done this, and have caused death or ulcers to the patient sometimes; and the constriction should be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that bad accidents may come to it, as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then poultices should not be placed on it; but wrap it with hard cloths instead of poultices, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see pus forming on the wound after one or two days, remove what you have placed over it with wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb must be positioned so that the pus runs down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but repeatedly forms pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, therefore you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all those detached pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in the area, or another form of corruption, you must treat it, according to what he said in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not remove it, for many times death comes from it, but let it rot; perhaps it will fall out after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the bruises that come over the healing
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We are often afflicted by bruises after the injury, especially when it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb is unpleasant to see; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the bruise is fresh: administer styptic medicines, like aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, as you may take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or with egg white or vinegar; and place them on the bruise in bandages, and bind it well, and do not unbind it for many days; and then unbind it, and start another, until the bruise is gone; or bind it over a piece of well-made lead; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the bruise has already hardened like a stone, and it needs to be removed, cut it off, and remove the excess that is visible; or scrape it with a scraper, until it is removed, and heal it until it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the broken bone is restored, and the limb remains weak and fragile afterward, it happens for many reasons: one of which is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or due to excessive washing; or due to too much movement, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body strong, so that the blood is multiplied within him; and give him baths, and give him joy and happiness; then put poultices on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and wash it often with warm water, so that nourishment flows to the limb; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb crooked after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is crooked after the restoration, and the broken bone is evident, and the limb's shape is unsightly, nevertheless, it does not entirely lose its natural function:  Do not believe the foolish who say one should break the limb again, and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great harm comes of it, and perhaps death; however, if the knots and twisting are recent, then they should be washed with hot water, or softening herbs should be cooked, like mallow leaves, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening poultice, such as well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of mallow and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a poultice on top; or take fat figs and crush them with fine flaxseed, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed by continually rubbing with wet hands for a long time.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And movement should be administered to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is old and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with an iron, then it must be cut down to the bone, with a sharp, light incisor; and great care and study should be put into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, so it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it should be immediately repositioned without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the area swells, and perhaps it is difficult to return it to its place; therefore, one should not move it when it is swollen: many times it causes inflammation and other pains; however, when this happens, bleed the patient, then leave it until the swelling subsides; then bathe the limb in warm water and oil, then gently reposition it, and treat each limb as it is brought back into place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Often the jaws are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is according to two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place, and slightly loosened; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and saliva drips from the mouth that he cannot hold, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, you must reset it quickly and not delay; and in such a way that the attendant holds the patient's head, and the attendant places the thumb of one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of both sides; and the other fingers of the hand should be used, for putting in balance; and instruct the patient to loosen their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the attendant puts it in balance, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the resetting is difficult, especially if it is both jaws together, then lubricate them with warm water and oil, until you reset them easily; and do not delay in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without forcing, then apply wet cloths in a plaster made of rose oil and wax, and then bind it lightly with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on their back, and their head be supported between two pillows, so that they do not move it to the right or left, nor make any effort to chew, but take light food, until the pain is gone, and the jaws are healed; and then let them eat whatever they wish lightly, and do not work to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is completely healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put right at once, and are not returned to their place, then fever and other customary illnesses arise, and perhaps a loose bowel, and perhaps vomiting clear phlegm.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is death; and many times the one who experiences it dies within four days.
de la forcelle	of the fork/pitchfork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot dislocate from the ribs within the continuation of the body and the breast, and it is sometimes dislocated outwards, and this is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and stretches their arms; and then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it; and the shoulder that is near the ribs cannot be dislocated; it is rare; and if it dislocates sometimes, return it to its place, as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it, and tell the patient to rest until they are healthy; and in the same way is the shoulder restored, when it is separated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one is that it dislocates towards the armpit below; the second is towards the breast; and perhaps it dislocates above, and this is rare; and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside by the nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those with little flesh, for in them it jumps quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps in some men there is a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary then that you examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocation is recognized when it is downwards towards the armpit, and a difference is noted between the diseased and healthy shoulder, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and under the armpit when touching the head of the shoulder, just as if it were a bone; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move with any movement; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly when touching; and this type of dislocation is merely to be reset, when it is new, or if the patient is a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister should lift the patient's hand upwards, then place their palms under the armpit, and raise the joint upwards forcefully to its place; and the minister should lift the hand and extend it upwards, then place it underneath; it will return quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the minister should apply a softening and soothing lotion, such as a decoction of elder, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and apply it; then the patient should be placed on their back, and a piece of wool the same thickness, not too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the armpit, then the minister should place their heel on the wool, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the patient's hand; and another minister should hold the patient's head, so that it does not move downwards; that shoulder returns immediately, and if you wish to reset it in this way: you should have a person present who is taller than the patient; and they should stand straight towards the side, and place their shoulder under the patient's armpit, and raise the armpit upwards, so that the patient hangs on it; and another minister should pull the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then something heavy should be placed with them, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset also in another way: and this is done by placing a long piece of wood in the ground, whose head is as round as a pestle, and it is neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but with soft cloths on top, and the patient is lying on the length of the stick; then the patient's hand is extended downwards to the other side forcefully, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not wish to return by all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take a stick of two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a round head so that it can be inserted deeply under the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie soft cloths over the top of the stick, so that the stick does not injure the patient, then place it under the patient's armpit; and extend their arm along the length of the stick, and tie the shoulder onto the stick, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a ladder of suitable width, and let the hand hang downwards, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will return to its place immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever way, you should place a wool pad under the armpit, then apply a prepared plaster of mill powder, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it, then bind it tightly under the armpit, and wrap the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to the neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal sooner; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and it is not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is displaced from its place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cauteries to three openings, as it is shown in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise the arm, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations towards the breast, or behind, are caused by pushing and stretching of the hands, and another bandage is applied; and treat until healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if, after healing, there is stiffness in the limb, and delay in movement, the patient should use baths many times, until the stiffness is relieved, and it returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation of the ribs
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the ribs is dislocated in points, and returns in points; and if dislocated on all sides, and especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reduced, because it is clearly seen and felt; and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased rib with the healthy one, you can clearly see it.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and the arm cannot bend, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before pus comes, for if pus were to come, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than the other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death results.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that it can be reset, that you stretch his hand with your two hands; and his arms be spread, and the hands of the mirror according to the rib, around, above and below, and place the joint against his shoulders together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and grasps the rib that is dislocated with the root of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer a strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm in each direction, after you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when the mirror has joined the joint to his hand, grease it with oil to soften the joint, then firmly place the joint so that it returns; and when it is in place, place a dry plaster with a little egg, and firmly bind it, and hang the arm from the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well aligned, reapply the plaster and bandage, and leave it thus for several days, until it is firmly in place; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset, and it moves, bathe and rub it gently, and press until it is relieved; or you place a greasy sheepskin on the joint, then leave it one day and one night, then remove it and have him enter a bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the sheepskin, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until he is healthy; and if you wish, place moist, warm cow manure with butter on it, and bind it; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is easier than other joints.  However, it must be put back in place quickly, at the moment it dislocates, before the area swells or a hot abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is done by placing the injured hand on a table, and the attendant extends the hand and aligns it, so that the palm is placed over the appearance of the joint, and pushed until it returns. However, you must check if it is properly in place; then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table during the extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, the patient places the back of their hand on the table, and the attendant places their hand over that area of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well.  If not, apply soothing plasters to any hot abscesses, and leave it as it is without trying again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot tolerate it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint remains crooked.  It does not harm the patient much, except that the hand is weakened and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves or arteries are severed; there is no other remedy than cautery near the affected area, and perhaps nothing else will work.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we have mentioned, then bandage it and leave it for five days, then unwrap it and leave it as it is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, soak it in hot water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated to either side, sometimes on the back of the palm or the front; then stretch the finger, and push the dislocation with your fingers until it returns, then support the head of the finger and bend it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then put it in the same position that day; and at night tie it, as we said, and untie it during the day, and move it, and re-tie it at night; and do this often, until it is straight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the front of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or the neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death quickly overtakes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that urination occurs involuntarily, and cannot be controlled, and often some limb is weakened, or both thighs or both arms or one.  And often the spine moves in four directions; that which moves backward is called "gibbosity." The treatment is to consider whether the gibbosity came about in childhood; if so, there is no cure or full recovery.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient healers described cures in grand terms, though there isn't much profit in all of them; but I have summarized them according to my intent, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in gibbosity that comes to the front of the chest, there is no remedy or health; and likewise, that which comes directly to both sides cannot be cured except that which comes to the back, as I have said; and is that the patient be laid flat on a level surface, and have padding underneath, so he is not injured; then put a burning brand into the ground at the head and another at the feet, and bind a bandage under the patient's armpits, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two assistants should hold the bandages, one at the head and the other at the feet, across the two burning brands; and they should be firmly held, the brands as we have said, and the healer should place their hands firmly on the spine, until it returns to its place.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board three arms long, and place it under the wall; and the patient should be on his side, and place the end of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and the healer should place their feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly, until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do it with a hand-operated winch.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should place two burning brands at the patient's head, one arm's length apart, and two others towards the feet, and have between each brand, above and below, a palm's width of space; and let there be a hole in each brand, through which the winch turns, and let the brands be firmly in the ground, so they do not move; and between each pair of brands have a rotating brand, on which the bandages turn, and have two small brands, one palm's length long, for turning the winch; and then tie the bandage that is under the armpits to the winch towards the head, and the other bandage towards the feet to the other winch, and each of the assistants turns their winch along the bandage, and the master places the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is straight, place a desiccant plaster with egg white, then bandages, and then a strip of a tablet three fingers long, which covers the area of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and the patient should use a mild diet until he is healed; and if anything comes up at the end of the healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the strip we have mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of lead is administered, and sometimes the appearance is in the lower back of the spine, and one thinks it is a dislocation; and it is the bone that is showing, for which one should not assume anything: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that at the joints of the hip and the shoulder, only dislocations occur, and not like at other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated in four ways: inward and outward, and forward and backward; and more inward than otherwise, and little forward or backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the sign of its inward dislocation is that when the sick leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee is more prominent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee towards the fire; and the area next to it is inflamed with a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh is displaced there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which occurs outward is that these symptoms are contrary to the previous ones.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that which happens forward are that they extend their leg fully, but do not bend the knee without pain, and if you want to make them walk, they cannot walk forward, and they retain their urine, and their groin swells, and when they walk, they step on their heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that which happens backward are that they cannot straighten or bend their knee, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is in the place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this type of dislocation is that you must observe if the dislocation is old, and it remains in its position, then there is no cure; and it is not appropriate to have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocation, you must hurry to turn the joint, and extend it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare two strong assistants, and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or with a rope tied above the knee; and another assistant extends their hand above in such a way that they place their hands below their armpits, then they tighten a soft rope above the thigh; and another holds the head of the rope; and they extend upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and hangs suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four types, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must apply treatment according to its type. When the dislocation is to the inside, you must place the patient on their healthy side, then put the rope around the root of the thigh, and the place below the armpit, then extend the rope upward towards the armpit, and towards the force; then another assistant, with their arms, grasps the large part of the affected thigh, and extends it outward forcefully: it will return to its place immediately; and this type of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot reduce it in this manner that we have said, you must tie the patient's two feet together with a strong soft rope around both ankles and both knees, and the affected leg should be extended two spans more than the other; then be suspended from the top of a post, and be two arms' length above the ground; then instruct an assistant to grasp the head of the thigh, and another assistant should hang with the patient, grasping the thigh firmly, because the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is outward, let the patient lie down, as we have said in those with gout, and tighten a rope around the affected leg and the foot also; then place two rods, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert a rod between the patient's thighs in the middle; and let them be covered with damp cloths around it so they do not harm the patient, then each assistant extends towards themselves, and the attendant must place the dislocation equal to their hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
